вҸә Done. The voyageai SDK is gone. Import time dropped from ~20s to 0.11s. What
  changed:

  - VoyageEmbedder (embed.py): import voyageai and voyageai.Client() replaced
  with self._api_key = os.environ.get("VOYAGE_API_KEY", "") and a new
  _call_voyage_embed() method that posts to api.voyageai.com/v1/embeddings via
  httpx. The _AdaptiveThrottle, checkpoint/resume, and Voyage Batch API code are
   all preserved вҖ” only the HTTP layer changed.
  - VoyageReranker (rerank.py): same pattern вҖ” stores API key at init, calls
  api.voyageai.com/v1/rerank directly in rerank().
  - pyproject.toml: removed voyageai>=0.3.0 from the full extra. httpx was
  already there.

вң» Worked for 9m 41s

      644 +                                                              
      645 +    Shown when ragrep is invoked with no args, or when the loc
          +al environment

          +.

          +_COLOR")

      654 +        return f"\033[{code}m{text}\033[0m" if use_color else 
          +text

          +d ragrep")

          +KEY, SLACK_TOKEN, etc.", "2"))

          +rep/issues")

вқҜ /ask lets plan, go or rust runtime                                            

вҸә Let me load the decision-gathering tool and sketch the decision space.

вҸә Before I write a plan, I need to nail down scope, motivation, and language вҖ”
  Go vs Rust is only one axis.

  The tradeoff landscape I see:

  The hot path that ships to end users is tiny: ragrep <query> loads faiss.index
   + chunks.pkl + bm25.pkl, runs dense + BM25 + RRF, hits Voyage rerank over
  HTTP, prints results. That's maybe 500 LOC of logic. The heavy stuff вҖ”
  scrapers, chunking, embedding, file extraction via Gemini, eval вҖ” is
  ingest-side and only the maintainer runs it.

  That split matters because a CLI-only rewrite is ~2 weeks and fixes the
  startup-latency class of problems forever, while leaving the messy ingest in
  Python. A full rewrite is 2-3 months because you'd re-implement scrapers,
  tokenization, file extraction, and ML toolchain in a non-Python ecosystem.

  On language, the directionally-honest picks:

  - Rust вҖ” matches the ripgrep/ruff/uv/tantivy lineage that ragrep is literally
  named after. Best FAISS + ML ecosystem (candle, ort, tantivy, usearch).
  Smallest binaries. Steeper curve. Solo-maintainer cost is real.
  - Go вҖ” faster to write and iterate, best-in-class cross-compilation, excellent
   HTTP stdlib. FAISS bindings exist but are thinner. ML ecosystem is weak вҖ”
  would bite hard if scope grows to embed/rerank locally. go install 
  ragrep.cc/cmd/ragrep@latest via the vanity domain go-import meta tag is a real
   bonus.

  My lean is Rust + CLI-only because (a) the branding alignment is real and
  marketable, (b) ingest-in-Python is fine for the solo-maintainer for now, and
  (c) if scope ever grows (local embeddings/reranking), Rust's ML story is
  dramatically better than Go's. But that's conditional on what you're actually
  optimizing for, so let me ask.

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· Go or Rust? вҶ’ Rust (Recommended)
     В· What scope should the rewrite cover? вҶ’ Full rewrite
     В· What's driving the rewrite? (pick all that apply) вҶ’ Single-binary 
     distribution, Startup latency

  вҺҝ В User rejected Claude's plan:
     в•ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв•®
     в”Ӯ Full Rust rewrite of ragrep                                             в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Context                                                                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ ragrep today is ~6,800 LOC of Python across 28 files, distributed via   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ curl ragrep.cc/install.sh | sh which calls uv tool install ragrep[full] в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  @ git+.... The user just shipped the public release. Two pain points   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ motivate this rewrite:                                                  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ 1. Startup latency. Even after the recent voyageai SDK вҶ’ httpx swap     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ that cut cold-import from ~20s to ~110ms, every Python invocation pays  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ ~100ms+ of import overhead before the first useful instruction. A       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ native binary starts in <10ms.                                          в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ 2. Single-binary distribution. Today users need uv (which installs      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Python, which sets up a venv) before ragrep exists on PATH. A static    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ binary skips all of that вҖ” same shape as ripgrep, ruff, uv, bun, deno.  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ The user picked Rust, full rewrite, motivated by startup latency +      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ single-binary distribution. The ragrep name on crates.io is taken       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ (active, v0.2.0, Nov 2025) so we ship via the vanity-domain installer,  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ not cargo install. The branding alignment with ripgrep/ruff/uv/tantivy  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ is a bonus.                                                             в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ This plan is the rewrite. It's substantial вҖ” ~10вҖ“12 weeks part-time вҖ”   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ so it's phased to ship value early (Phase 1 = working CLI binary        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ against an existing Python-built index) and let ingest catch up later.  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ On-disk reality (what we're migrating from)                             в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ data/index/  вҶ’  1.3 GB total                                            в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ   faiss.index    404 MB    FAISS native binary    PORTABLE вҖ” Rust       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ faiss-rs reads same format                                              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ   chunks.pkl     203 MB    Python pickle of list[Chunk]    must convert в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  (msgpack)                                                              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ   bm25.pkl       185 MB    Python pickle of BM25Okapi      must rebuild в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  from chunks via Rust BM25                                              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ   embed_cache.pkl 485 MB   Python pickle of dict[sha256, vec]   must    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ convert (msgpack)                                                       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ faiss.index is the only directly-portable artifact. The three pickles   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ need a one-shot Python migration script that runs in the existing venv, в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  reads the pickles, and writes msgpack equivalents. bm25.pkl is dropped в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  (it's just bag-of-words counts; we rebuild it cheaply from             в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ chunks.msgpack).                                                        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Crate layout                                                            в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Single Cargo workspace at the repo root:                                в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ ragrep/                                                                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”ңв”Җв”Җ Cargo.toml                       # workspace                        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”ңв”Җв”Җ crates/                                                             в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ragrep-core/                 # types, config, store, retrieve,  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ rerank, embed-http, generate                                            в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ragrep-scrape/               # slack, atlassian, gdrive, git,   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ bitbucket, code (one mod each)                                          в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ragrep-extract/              # PDF/DOCX/PPTX/XLSX вҶ’ text via    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Gemini multimodal HTTP                                                  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ragrep-eval/                 # entity_graph + harness           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ragrep-server/               # axum HTTP server (binary)        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ ragrep-cli/                  # clap CLI (binary, the `ragrep`   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ shipped to users)                                                       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”ңв”Җв”Җ tools/                                                              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ migrate_index.py             # one-shot Python:                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ chunks.pkl/embed_cache.pkl вҶ’ msgpack                                    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в””в”Җв”Җ docs/                            # unchanged: install.sh,           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ index.html, fonts/                                                      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Why this split: ragrep-cli and ragrep-server are the two ship targets.  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Everything else is a library crate, so cross-binary code (e.g.          в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ retrieval) lives in ragrep-core. Scrapers go in their own crate because в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  they pull source-specific HTTP/auth deps (git2, OAuth flows) that the  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ CLI binary shouldn't link.                                              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Library picks (and why)                                                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ

     в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ                                                                    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Scope cut: local model providers (regression flagged)                   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Current Python supports provider = "sentence-transformers" for both     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ embedding and reranking (loads Qwen3-Embedding-0.6B /                   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Qwen3-Reranker-0.6B locally via PyTorch). v1 Rust drops this: HTTP-only в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  providers (Voyage, OpenAI, Gemini for embed; Voyage for rerank).       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Reason: replacing it requires candle or ort + ONNX-converted models +   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ GPU/MPS feature detection. That's 3+ weeks of work for a feature only   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ used when users have no API keys. Better to ship v1 without it and add  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ v2 as a feature flag.                                                   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Migration note for affected users: switch provider = "voyage" in        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ config.toml and add VOYAGE_API_KEY to .env. Voyage gives 200M tokens    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ free/month.                                                             в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Phased delivery                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Phase 0 вҖ” scaffolding (1 week)                                          в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - Cargo workspace, all 6 crates with empty lib.rs/main.rs               в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - GitHub Actions matrix: x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu,                      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ aarch64-apple-darwin, x86_64-apple-darwin, aarch64-unknown-linux-gnu,   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ x86_64-pc-windows-msvc                                                  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - target/release/ragrep --help builds and runs on all targets           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - Updated docs/install.sh: detects platform via uname, downloads from   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ GitHub Releases, verifies sha256, installs to ~/.local/bin/ragrep.      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Falls back to uv tool install only if --legacy is passed (transition    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ window)                                                                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Verify: cross build --target $TGT succeeds for all 5 targets in CI;     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ target/release/ragrep --help returns in <50ms wall.                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Phase 1 вҖ” query path (2 weeks)                                          в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::models (serde-friendly mirrors of Document, Chunk,       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ SearchResult)                                                           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::config (reads config.toml, env file search same as       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Python)                                                                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::store::load (msgpack chunks, FAISS via faiss-rs,         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ hand-rolled BM25)                                                       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::retrieve (port dense_search, bm25_search,                в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ _reciprocal_rank_fusion, _multi_signal_rrf)                             в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::rerank::voyage (httpx вҶ’ reqwest port; same JSON shape)   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::embed::{voyage,openai,gemini} (HTTP only, no SDK)        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::search::{grep, semantic, hybrid} (matches Python's       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ search.py API surface)                                                  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-cli::main (clap with full argparse parity: -n, -s, -m, -f      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ KEY=VAL, --after, --before, -c, --full, --json, --scores, --metadata,   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ --server, --config)                                                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-cli::splash (port the ASCII splash from cli.py)                в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-cli::server_proxy (port _query_server, including Cloud Run     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ identity-token via gcloud auth print-identity-token)                    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - tools/migrate_index.py: reads existing chunks.pkl and                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ embed_cache.pkl, writes msgpack. Drops bm25.pkl (rebuilt by ragrep      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ ingest)                                                                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-cli::cmd_rebuild_bm25: one-time helper that loads              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ chunks.msgpack, builds BM25, writes bm25.msgpack (bridge for users who  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ haven't re-ingested)                                                    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Verify (parity test): pick 50 representative queries (mix of grep,      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ semantic, hybrid; mix of source filters and date filters). Run them     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ through Python ragrep, capture top-10 chunk IDs. Run same queries       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ through Rust ragrep against the same index. Top-10 sets should match    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ exactly for grep mode and have вүҘ9/10 overlap for semantic/hybrid        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ (allowing for floating-point drift in cosine scores). Script:           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ tools/parity_test.sh.                                                   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Ship gate: at end of Phase 1, the binary is usable end-to-end against   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ an existing Python-built index. We can release this as v0.2.0 and let   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ users start benefiting from the startup-latency win immediately.        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Phase 2 вҖ” ingest pipeline (3 weeks)                                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::chunk (tiktoken-rs, 512 tokens, 64 overlap, port         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ chunk_all)                                                              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::normalize (one normalizer per source вҖ” port              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ normalize.py's 526 LOC of source-specific logic)                        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::embed_cache (msgpack-backed sha256 вҶ’ Vec)                в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::embed::voyage::embed_documents (port _AdaptiveThrottle,  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ batch size 16, checkpoint every 500 batches, retry-after parsing)       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::store::save (FAISS IndexFlatIP build + write, BM25 build в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  + write, chunks msgpack write)                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-core::pipeline::ingest (orchestrate normalize вҶ’ chunk вҶ’ dedup  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ вҶ’ embed вҶ’ store; incremental via embed_cache)                           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-cli::cmd_ingest (ragrep ingest [--force] [--source X])         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Verify: re-ingest the existing data/raw/ end-to-end. Compare new        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ chunks.msgpack count vs old chunks.pkl (same), new faiss.index ntotal   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ vs old (same), and run the Phase-1 parity test against the              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ freshly-Rust-built index.                                               в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Phase 3 вҖ” scrapers (3 weeks)                                            в”Ӯ

     в”Ӯ - ragrep-cli::cmd_scrape (ragrep scrape [--source slack,git,...])       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Verify: each scraper produces NDJSON in data/raw/{source}/              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ byte-identical (modulo timestamps) to the Python equivalent for at      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ least 100 real records. Diff with jq -S to ignore key ordering.         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ

     в”Ӯ RAGREP_GCS_BUCKET set)                                                  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-eval::entity_graph (port entity_graph.py вҖ” Jira-ID extraction  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ only, since service-pattern was stripped)                               в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-eval::harness (port harness.py, source_recall / entity_recall  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ / MRR per stage)                                                        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - ragrep-cli::cmd_eval and cmd_stats and cmd_inspect                    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - Cloud Run deploy script update: build aarch64-unknown-linux-gnu       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ binary, package in distroless container                                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Verify: run ragrep eval against existing index; numbers should match    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ the Python baseline within Вұ1pp on each metric. make serve-rust && curl в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  localhost:8321/search?q=auth&mode=grep returns same JSON shape as      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Python.                                                                 в”Ӯ

     в”Ӯ в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Ө                                                                     в”Ӯ

     в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Ө                                                                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ Server cold start (Cloud Run,  в”Ӯ ~3 min   в”Ӯ ~2 min (dominated by GCS  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ                                                                     в”Ӯ

     в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Ө                                                                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ Binary size (stripped, single  в”Ӯ n/a      в”Ӯ <30 MB                    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ                                                                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Ӯ arch)                          в”Ӯ          в”Ӯ                           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ                                                                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”ҳ                                                                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Risks & mitigations                                                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - faiss-rs ergonomics. Bindings are thin and docs are sparse.           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Mitigation: Phase 1 starts with a 1-day spike that loads the existing   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ faiss.index and runs a single search. If it stalls, fall back to        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ usearch (different format, requires Phase-1 reindex). Decision point    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ inside Phase 1, week 1.                                                 в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - GDrive OAuth in Rust. yup-oauth2 requires either service-account JSON в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  (cleanest) or an installed-app flow with localhost callback.           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Mitigation: require service-account JSON for v1; document how to create в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  one. The Python path used gcloud auth application-default login which  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ is convenient for the user but harder to match in Rust without shelling в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  out.                                                                   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - Async/sync split in CLI. ragrep "query" doesn't need an async runtime в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  (one HTTP call to Voyage rerank). Spinning up tokio for that is        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ overkill (~5ms cost). Mitigation: ragrep-core::embed and ::rerank       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ expose both sync (ureq) and async (reqwest) variants; CLI uses sync,    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ server uses async.                                                      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - tiktoken vs Voyage tokenizer drift. Voyage uses its own tokenizer;    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ we'd be using cl100k_base. For chunk-size enforcement (512 tokens) the  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ drift is small (вүӨ5% chunk-count differences in practice). Mitigation:   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ accept the drift; chunks aren't required to be exactly 512 tokens. If   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Voyage rejects an oversize batch we already retry.                      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - Pickle migration robustness. The migration script must read whatever  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ pickle protocol Python wrote. Mitigation: the script runs in the user's в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  existing venv (which has the same pickle/Python version that wrote     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ it), so this is a non-issue. Document the venv requirement in           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ MIGRATION.md.                                                           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - Scope creep. 10вҖ“12 weeks part-time is a lot. Mitigation: Phase 1 is   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ the ship-gate. After Phase 1, users get the latency win immediately.    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Phases 2вҖ“5 can take as long as they take without blocking value.        в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Critical files to model the Rust port on                                в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - src/ragrep/models.py (61 LOC) вҖ” flat dataclasses, trivial mapping to  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ serde structs                                                           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - src/ragrep/config.py (159 LOC) вҖ” already does env-file + XDG search;  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ mirror in ragrep-core::config                                           в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - src/ragrep/ingest/store.py (140 LOC) вҖ” build_faiss_index, save_index, в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ  load_index, model_key, save_multi_index, load_multi_index. Direct      в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ ports.                                                                  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - src/ragrep/query/retrieve.py (222 LOC) вҖ” dense_search, bm25_search,   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ _reciprocal_rank_fusion, _multi_signal_rrf, retrieve, retrieve_multi.   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Algorithmic; direct ports.                                              в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - src/ragrep/search.py (244 LOC) вҖ” public API surface (search_grep,     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ search_semantic, search_hybrid). Matches the JSON the CLI/server emit.  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - src/ragrep/cli.py (777 LOC) вҖ” argparse surface to mirror in clap,     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ including the splash and server proxy.                                  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - src/ragrep/server.py (172 LOC) вҖ” /search endpoint shape to mirror in  в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ axum.                                                                   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - src/ragrep/ingest/embed.py (814 LOC) вҖ” VoyageEmbedder is the model    в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ for HTTP+throttle. The OpenAI/Gemini variants are similar shapes.       в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ - src/ragrep/ingest/scrape_slack.py (823 LOC) вҖ” biggest scraper, sets   в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ the bar for the scraper module's complexity budget.                     в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ                                                                         в”Ӯ
     в”Ӯ Verification recipe (end-to-end)                                        в”Ӯ

вқҜ /taste                                                                        

вҸә You're right to push back. Reading my own plan through the taste lens, the
  structure has problems. Let me diagnose before revising.

  Taste diagnosis

  Primary sins:

  1. Ancestry encoded into every crate. I wrote ragrep-core, ragrep-scrape,
  ragrep-extract, ragrep-eval, ragrep-server, ragrep-cli. The workspace is named
   ragrep. Every crate repeats the namespace. That's Cargo convention for
  published crates (no registry scopes) but this is an internal workspace вҖ”
  nothing publishes. The prefix is pure stutter.
  2. Two binaries when one would do. ragrep-cli + ragrep-server as separate
  binaries mirrors Python's accident (cli.py + server.py + uvicorn). ripgrep,
  ruff, uv, bun, deno all ship one binary with subcommands. ragrep serve is
  cleaner than shipping a second binary named ragrep-server.
  3. Workspace where a crate would do. 6 crates, each depending on ragrep-core.
  Three of them (scrape, extract, eval) are only used by the ingest path and by
  one binary. Compile-time isolation doesn't pay for itself at this size.
  4. cmd_* prefix. cmd_scrape, cmd_ingest, cmd_rebuild_bm25 inside what would be
   ragrep-cli/src/cli.rs вҖ” the path already says "this is a cli command."
  5. ragrep-core is a junk-drawer name. "Core" is the confession that I couldn't
   find a domain word. The crate contains models, config, store, retrieve,
  rerank, embed, generate вҖ” that's the whole engine. If it's the whole engine,
  it doesn't need a crate. If it's a layer, it needs a domain name.

  Taste-correct shape

  Single crate, one binary, subcommand surface. Path is the namespace.

  ragrep/
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ Cargo.toml                       # one crate, one [[bin]] name = "ragrep"
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ src/
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ main.rs                      # clap entry, dispatches to cli::*
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ lib.rs                       # module declarations
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ splash.rs
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ models.rs                    # Document, Chunk, SearchResult,
  QueryResult
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ config.rs                    # Config, load_config, load_env_files,
  find_config_path
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ store.rs                     # load/save faiss + chunks + bm25
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ chunk.rs                     # 512-token chunking
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ bm25.rs                      # hand-rolled BM25Okapi
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ retrieve.rs                  # dense + bm25 + rrf fusion
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ rerank.rs                    # voyage rerank

  hybrid)
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ pipeline.rs                  # scrapeвҶ’normalizeвҶ’chunkвҶ’embedвҶ’store
  orchestration
  в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ extract.rs                   # gemini multimodal HTTP

  bridge)
  в””в”Җв”Җ tools/
      в””в”Җв”Җ migrate.py                   # one-shot pickleвҶ’msgpack

  Reading the paths as namespaces

  - ragrep::embed::voyage вҖ” types like Embedder, functions like embed,
  embed_query. No stutter.
  - ragrep::scrape::slack вҖ” fn run, struct Config. The file name supplies the
  source.
  - ragrep::normalize::slack вҖ” fn normalize(raw: &Raw) -> Document. The parent
  normalize:: supplies the verb.
  - ragrep::cli::ingest вҖ” fn run(args: IngestArgs) -> Result<()>. The path says
  it's the ingest subcommand handler.
  - ragrep::serve::search вҖ” async fn handle(Query(q): Query<SearchQuery>) -> 
  Json<...>. The path says it's the /search serve handler.
  - ragrep::eval::entity вҖ” fn extract(chunk: &Chunk) -> Vec<Entity>.

  What collapses away

  What the binary looks like to users

  ragrep                          # welcome splash (no args)
  ragrep <term>                   # search (default, implicit subcommand)
  ragrep <term> -m grep -n 5      # search with flags
  ragrep serve --port 8321        # HTTP server
  ragrep ingest [--force]         # build index
  ragrep scrape --source slack,git
  ragrep eval
  ragrep stats
  ragrep inspect raw
  ragrep rebuild-bm25             # one-off bridge for pickle-migrated indexes

  One binary, one install, one --help tree. Matches rg, cargo, uv, bun.

  Why single crate, not workspace

  The case for a workspace was compile-time isolation вҖ” the CLI binary shouldn't
   link axum/tower. Resolution: feature flags in a single crate, if compile time
   becomes a real complaint. It won't for v1 (the whole repo is ~15k LOC of
  Rust; touches whole-crate recompile in <10s on cargo check).

  When the workspace actually pays for itself: publishing ragrep-retrieve as a
  standalone library someone else depends on. No current demand. Don't build for
   it.

  The one exception to "no stutter"

  cli/ as a directory name repeats what the whole project is (ragrep is a CLI).
  The taste rule says that's redundant. But the alternative вҖ” putting subcommand
   dispatchers at the top level (src/{search,serve,ingest,...}.rs) вҖ” conflicts
  with the engine modules (src/search.rs already exists). So cli/ earns its keep
   as a boundary between "user-facing subcommand handlers" and "engine building
  blocks that handlers call." I'll keep it.

      в””в”Җв”Җ rebuild_bm25.rs

  What changed

  - store.rs and bm25.rs moved under index/. They're both about the on-disk
  index; neither is ingest-specific or query-specific. index::store::save,
  index::bm25::Okapi.
  - retrieve.rs, rerank.rs, generate.rs moved under query/. They're read-side
  building blocks. query::retrieve::dense, query::rerank::voyage::rerank,
  query::generate.
  - search.rs dissolved into query/mod.rs. Instead of query::search::hybrid,
  it's query::hybrid вҖ” the query namespace already says "this is the public
  search surface." Callers write query::hybrid(&config, term).
  - chunk.rs, extract.rs, normalize/, scrape/, pipeline.rs moved under ingest/.
  All write-side. Mirrors the Python src/ragrep/ingest/ layout, with the bonus
  that scrape_atlassian.py-style flat filenames become
  ingest/scrape/atlassian.rs (proper hierarchy, not hyphenation).
  - Top-level keeps only what's genuinely universal. models, config, splash вҖ”
  used from everywhere, belong nowhere specific.
  - embed/ stays at the top because both ingest (batch) and query (one-shot)
  call it. Putting it under ingest/ would force query to import
  crate::ingest::embed вҖ” a write-side/read-side taboo.

  Namespace reads at call sites

  use crate::{config, embed, index, query, ingest, eval};

  let cfg = config::load(None)?;                             // shared
  let embedder = embed::voyage::Embedder::new(&cfg)?;        // shared
  let (faiss, chunks, bm25) = index::store::load(&cfg.index_dir)?;  // read side
  let results = query::hybrid(&cfg, "auth", 5, ...)?;        // read side
  let q_vec = embedder.embed_query("auth")?;                 // shared
  let ranked = query::retrieve::rrf(&dense, &bm25_hits);     // read side
  let reranked = query::rerank::voyage::rerank(query, docs).await?;

  // ingest path
  let stats = ingest::pipeline::run(&cfg, force)?;           // write side
  let docs = ingest::normalize::slack::all(&raw_dir)?;       // write side
  let chunked = ingest::chunk::all(&docs, 512, 64);          // write side
  let embeddings = embed::voyage::batch(&chunked, &cache).await?;

  The paths tell you read vs. write vs. shared. No concept appears twice in any
  full path.

     Full Rust rewrite of ragrep

     Context

     ragrep today is ~6,800 LOC of Python across 28 files, distributed via curl 
     ragrep.cc/install.sh | sh which calls uv tool install ragrep[full] @ 
     git+.... The user just shipped the public release. Two pain points motivate
      this rewrite:

     1. Startup latency. Even after the recent voyageai SDK вҶ’ httpx swap that
     cut cold-import from ~20s to ~110ms, every Python invocation pays ~100ms+
     of import overhead before the first useful instruction. A native binary
     starts in <10ms.
     2. Single-binary distribution. Today users need uv (which installs Python,
     which sets up a venv) before ragrep exists on PATH. A static binary skips
     all of that вҖ” same shape as ripgrep, ruff, uv, bun, deno.

     The user picked Rust, full rewrite, motivated by startup latency + 
     single-binary distribution. The ragrep name on crates.io is taken (active,
     v0.2.0, Nov 2025) so we ship via the vanity-domain installer, not cargo 
     install. The branding alignment with ripgrep/ruff/uv/tantivy is a bonus.

     This plan is the rewrite. It's substantial вҖ” ~10вҖ“12 weeks part-time вҖ” so
     it's phased to ship value early (Phase 1 = working CLI binary against an
     existing Python-built index) and let ingest catch up later.

     On-disk reality (what we're migrating from)

     data/index/  вҶ’  1.3 GB total
       faiss.index    404 MB    FAISS native binary    PORTABLE вҖ” Rust faiss-rs
     reads same format
       chunks.pkl     203 MB    Python pickle of list[Chunk]    must convert
     (msgpack)
       bm25.pkl       185 MB    Python pickle of BM25Okapi      must rebuild
     from chunks via Rust BM25
       embed_cache.pkl 485 MB   Python pickle of dict[sha256, vec]   must
     convert (msgpack)

     faiss.index is the only directly-portable artifact. The three pickles need
     a one-shot Python migration script that runs in the existing venv, reads
     the pickles, and writes msgpack equivalents. bm25.pkl is dropped (it's just
      bag-of-words counts; we rebuild it cheaply from chunks.msgpack).

     Module layout

     Single crate, one binary, subcommand surface. The path is the namespace;
     nothing in the tree repeats ragrep.

     ragrep/
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ Cargo.toml                       # one crate, one [[bin]] name =
     "ragrep"
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ src/
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ main.rs                      # clap entry; dispatches to cli::*
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ lib.rs                       # module declarations
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ splash.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ models.rs                    # shared: Document, Chunk,
     SearchResult, QueryResult
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ config.rs                    # shared: Config, load, env + XDG
     search
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ embed/                       # shared capability (ingest batches;
     query one-shots)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs                   # Embedder trait + factory
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ voyage.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ openai.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ gemini.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ cache.rs                 # content-hash вҶ’ vec
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ throttle.rs              # adaptive rate-limit throttle
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ index/                       # on-disk persistence (both sides
     touch)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ store.rs                 # load/save faiss + chunks + bm25
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ bm25.rs                  # hand-rolled Okapi data structure
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ingest/                      # write side
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ pipeline.rs              # scrape вҶ’ normalize вҶ’ chunk вҶ’ embed вҶ’
      store
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ chunk.rs                 # 512-token chunking
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ extract.rs               # gemini multimodal HTTP for
     PDF/DOCX/PPTX/XLSX
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ normalize/
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ slack.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ atlassian.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ gdrive.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ git.rs

     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ serve/                       # HTTP server (backs `ragrep serve`)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs                   # axum router
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ auth.rs                  # Cloud Run JWT middleware
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ search.rs                # GET /search handler
     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ cli/                         # subcommand dispatchers (user
     boundary)
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs                   # Subcommand enum + dispatch
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ search.rs                # `ragrep <term>` default
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ serve.rs                 # `ragrep serve`
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ ingest.rs
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ scrape.rs
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ eval.rs
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ stats.rs
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ inspect.rs
     в”Ӯ       в””в”Җв”Җ rebuild_bm25.rs          # transient bridge for pickle-migrated
      indexes
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ tools/
     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ migrate.py                   # one-shot pickle вҶ’ msgpack
     в””в”Җв”Җ docs/                            # unchanged: install.sh, index.html,
     fonts/

     How paths read as namespaces

     Read vs write vs shared is legible from the tree alone:

     - embed::voyage вҖ” shared capability. Embedder, embed, embed_query.
     - index::store::load вҖ” on-disk, both sides touch.
     - index::bm25::Okapi вҖ” the BM25 data structure type.
     - ingest::scrape::slack::run вҖ” write-side, API fetch, source-specific.
     - ingest::normalize::slack::normalize вҖ” write-side, raw JSON вҶ’ Document.
     - ingest::chunk::all вҖ” write-side step.
     - ingest::pipeline::run вҖ” write-side orchestrator.
     - query::hybrid вҖ” public engine API; top-level in query::.
     - query::retrieve::dense, query::retrieve::rrf вҖ” retrieval building blocks.
     - query::rerank::voyage::rerank вҖ” rerank building block.
     - cli::ingest::run вҖ” CLI subcommand handler.
     - serve::search::handle вҖ” HTTP endpoint handler.
     - eval::entity::extract вҖ” entity extraction for eval.

     No concept appears twice in any full path. The write/read/shared split is
     inferable without opening a single file.

     User-facing surface

     One binary, clap subcommands (mirrors ripgrep/cargo/uv):

     ragrep                              # welcome splash (no args)
     ragrep <term>                       # search (default, implicit subcommand)
     ragrep <term> -m grep -n 5
     ragrep serve --port 8321            # HTTP server (replaces FastAPI)
     ragrep ingest [--force]
     ragrep scrape --source slack,git
     ragrep eval
     ragrep stats
     ragrep inspect raw
     ragrep rebuild-bm25                 # one-off bridge for pickle-migrated
     indexes

     Why single crate

     The case for a workspace was compile-time isolation вҖ” the CLI binary
     shouldn't link axum. Resolution: feature flags in a single crate if compile
      time becomes a real complaint. It won't for v1 (total Rust LOC lands
     around 15k; whole-crate cargo check stays under 10s on modern hardware). A
     workspace would earn its keep when another project depends on
     ragrep-retrieve as a library. No such demand today.

     Taste exceptions taken

     - cli/ as a directory repeats the project identity (ragrep is a CLI).
     Alternative was putting subcommand dispatchers flat at
     src/{search,serve,ingest,...}.rs, which collides with the engine modules of
      the same names. cli/ earns the exception as a boundary between
     "user-facing subcommand handlers" and "engine building blocks those
     handlers call."
     - tools/migrate.py stays Python because it runs inside the user's existing
     venv to read pickle format. Cross-language script in the tools/ boundary is
      correct.

     Library picks (and why)

     в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

     в”Ӯ handling      в”Ӯ                      в”Ӯ ingest runs                      в”Ӯ
     в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

     Scope cut: local model providers (regression flagged)

     Current Python supports provider = "sentence-transformers" for both
     embedding and reranking (loads Qwen3-Embedding-0.6B / Qwen3-Reranker-0.6B
     locally via PyTorch). v1 Rust drops this: HTTP-only providers (Voyage,
     OpenAI, Gemini for embed; Voyage for rerank).

     Reason: replacing it requires candle or ort + ONNX-converted models +
     GPU/MPS feature detection. That's 3+ weeks of work for a feature only used
     when users have no API keys. Better to ship v1 without it and add v2 as a
     feature flag.

     Migration note for affected users: switch provider = "voyage" in
     config.toml and add VOYAGE_API_KEY to .env. Voyage gives 200M tokens
     free/month.

     Phased delivery

     Phase 0 вҖ” scaffolding (1 week)

     - Single crate at repo root, empty main.rs/lib.rs, clap skeleton with every
      subcommand wired to a stub
     - GitHub Actions matrix: x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu, aarch64-apple-darwin,
     x86_64-apple-darwin, aarch64-unknown-linux-gnu, x86_64-pc-windows-msvc
     - Updated docs/install.sh: detects platform via uname, downloads from
     GitHub Releases, verifies sha256, installs to ~/.local/bin/ragrep. Falls
     back to uv tool install only if --legacy is passed (transition window)

     Verify: cross build --target $TGT succeeds for all 5 targets in CI;
     target/release/ragrep --help returns in <50ms wall.

     Phase 1 вҖ” query path (2 weeks)

     - models вҖ” serde mirrors of Document, Chunk, SearchResult, QueryResult
     - config вҖ” reads config.toml, env file + XDG search (mirror of config.py)
     - index::bm25 вҖ” hand-rolled Okapi data structure
     - index::store вҖ” msgpack chunks, FAISS via faiss crate, load/save
     - query::retrieve вҖ” fn dense, fn bm25, fn rrf, fn multi_signal_rrf
     - query::rerank::voyage вҖ” reqwest port of the recently-ported httpx rerank
     call
     - embed::{voyage, openai, gemini} вҖ” HTTP only, no SDK
     - query::{grep, semantic, hybrid} вҖ” public engine API, top-level fns in
     query/mod.rs
     - cli::search::run вҖ” clap args mirror argparse 1:1 (-n, -s, -m, -f KEY=VAL,
      --after, --before, -c, --full, --json, --scores, --metadata, --server,
     --config)
     - splash вҖ” port the ASCII splash; same trigger conditions
     - cli::search::proxy вҖ” port _query_server, including Cloud Run
     identity-token via gcloud auth print-identity-token
     - tools/migrate.py вҖ” reads existing chunks.pkl and embed_cache.pkl, writes
     msgpack. Drops bm25.pkl (rebuild handled below)
     - cli::rebuild_bm25::run вҖ” one-time helper; loads chunks.msgpack, builds
     BM25, writes bm25.msgpack. Transitional, goes away once Phase 2 ingest can
     do this.

     Verify (parity test): pick 50 representative queries (mix of grep,
     semantic, hybrid; mix of source filters and date filters). Run them through
      Python ragrep, capture top-10 chunk IDs. Run the same queries through Rust
      ragrep against the same index. Top-10 sets match exactly for grep, вүҘ9/10
     overlap for semantic/hybrid (floating-point drift). Script:
     tools/parity.sh.

     Ship gate: end of Phase 1, the binary is usable against an existing
     Python-built index. Release as v0.2.0; users get the startup-latency win
     immediately.

     Phase 2 вҖ” ingest pipeline (3 weeks)

     - ingest::chunk вҖ” tiktoken-rs, 512 tokens, 64 overlap
     - ingest::normalize::{slack, atlassian, gdrive, git, bitbucket, code, file}
      вҖ” one submodule per source (port normalize.py's 526 LOC)
     - embed::cache вҖ” msgpack-backed HashMap<Sha256, Vec<f32>>
     - embed::throttle вҖ” port _AdaptiveThrottle: initial 30s, 0.75Г— on 3-streak
     success, 1.5Г— on 429, floor erosion every 10 successes near floor
     - embed::voyage::batch вҖ” reuses throttle, checkpoints every 500 batches,
     retry-after parsing
     - index::store::save вҖ” FAISS IndexFlatIP build + write, BM25 build + write,
      chunks msgpack write
     - ingest::pipeline::run вҖ” normalize вҶ’ chunk вҶ’ dedup вҶ’ embed вҶ’ store;
     incremental via embed::cache
     - cli::ingest::run вҖ” ragrep ingest [--force] [--source X]

     Verify: re-ingest the existing data/raw/ end-to-end. New chunks.msgpack
     count matches old chunks.pkl; new faiss.index ntotal matches; Phase-1
     parity test passes against the Rust-built index.

     Phase 3 вҖ” scrapers (3 weeks)

     - ingest::scrape::git вҖ” git2 bindings, port scrape_git.py. Do first as
     proof вҖ” easiest source.
     - ingest::scrape::slack вҖ” raw HTTP to api.slack.com/api/* with pagination,
     threads, bookmarks, pins, files (port the 823-LOC scrape_slack.py)
     - ingest::scrape::atlassian вҖ” Confluence pages + Jira issues + comments via
      basic auth
     - ingest::scrape::bitbucket вҖ” OAuth client-creds flow, PR descriptions +
     comments
     - ingest::scrape::gdrive вҖ” yup-oauth2 service account or ADC, list +
     download docs/sheets/slides/PDFs
     - ingest::scrape::code вҖ” file walking + extension filter
     - ingest::extract вҖ” PDF/DOCX/PPTX/XLSX вҶ’ text via Gemini multimodal HTTP
     (port extract.py)
     - cli::scrape::run вҖ” ragrep scrape [--source slack,git,...]

     Verify: each scraper produces NDJSON in data/raw/{source}/ byte-identical
     (modulo timestamps) to the Python equivalent for вүҘ100 real records. Diff
     with jq -S to ignore key ordering.

     Phase 4 вҖ” server + eval (2 weeks)

     Risks & mitigations

     - faiss-rs ergonomics. Bindings are thin and docs are sparse. Mitigation:
     Phase 1 starts with a 1-day spike that loads the existing faiss.index and
     runs a single search. If it stalls, fall back to usearch (different format,
      requires Phase-1 reindex). Decision point inside Phase 1, week 1.
     - GDrive OAuth in Rust. yup-oauth2 requires either service-account JSON
     (cleanest) or an installed-app flow with localhost callback. Mitigation:
     require service-account JSON for v1; document how to create one. The Python
      path used gcloud auth application-default login which is convenient for
     the user but harder to match in Rust without shelling out.
     - Async/sync split in CLI. ragrep "query" doesn't need an async runtime
     (one HTTP call to Voyage rerank). Spinning up tokio for that is overkill
     (~5ms cost). Mitigation: embed:: and rerank:: expose both sync (ureq) and
     async (reqwest) variants; the CLI search path uses sync, the serve
     subcommand uses async.
     - tiktoken vs Voyage tokenizer drift. Voyage uses its own tokenizer; we'd
     be using cl100k_base. For chunk-size enforcement (512 tokens) the drift is
     small (вүӨ5% chunk-count differences in practice). Mitigation: accept the
     drift; chunks aren't required to be exactly 512 tokens. If Voyage rejects
     an oversize batch we already retry.
     - Pickle migration robustness. The migration script must read whatever
     pickle protocol Python wrote. Mitigation: the script runs in the user's
     existing venv (which has the same pickle/Python version that wrote it), so
     this is a non-issue. Document the venv requirement in MIGRATION.md.
     - Scope creep. 10вҖ“12 weeks part-time is a lot. Mitigation: Phase 1 is the
     ship-gate. After Phase 1, users get the latency win immediately. Phases 2вҖ“5
      can take as long as they take without blocking value.

     Verification recipe (end-to-end)

     After Phase 1 ships:

     # Build for current platform
     cargo build --release

     # Smoke test
     ./target/release/ragrep --help                          # <20ms expected
     ./target/release/ragrep                                 # shows splash

     # Migrate Python pickles to msgpack (one-time)
     python tools/migrate.py data/index/

     # Parity test against Python
     ./tools/parity_test.sh                                  # 50 queries, вүҘ90% 
     top-10 overlap

     # End-to-end search
     ./target/release/ragrep "auth" -m grep -n 5
     ./target/release/ragrep "auth" -m hybrid -n 5
     ./target/release/ragrep "auth" --json | jq

     # Server mode (uses existing Python server)
     RAGREP_SERVER=http://localhost:8321 ./target/release/ragrep "auth"

     # Cross-compile sanity
     cross build --release --target aarch64-apple-darwin
     cross build --release --target x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu

     After Phase 5 ships:

     # From clean Docker
     docker run --rm -it debian:bookworm-slim bash -c \
       "apt-get update && apt-get install -y curl ca-certificates && \
        curl -fsSL https://ragrep.cc/install.sh | sh && \
        ~/.local/bin/ragrep --help && \
        RAGREP_SERVER=https://your-cloud-run.run.app ~/.local/bin/ragrep 'auth'"

     What stays after Phase 5

     - docs/ (landing page, install.sh, fonts) вҖ” unchanged content, install.sh
     now downloads binary
     - tools/migrate.py вҖ” kept indefinitely so old-Python users can still
     migrate
     - config.toml format вҖ” same TOML shape, fully readable by Rust
     - .env / .env.example вҖ” same env vars
     - data/index/ layout вҖ” same files, msgpack instead of pickle for
     chunks/embed_cache
     - GitHub repo URL (github.com/fntune/ragrep) вҖ” same
     - Vanity domain (ragrep.cc) вҖ” same

     What goes:
     - pyproject.toml, src/ragrep/, uv.lock, Makefile (replaced by justfile or
     just cargo commands)
     - requirements.txt Cloud Run target (replaced by Dockerfile building the
     Rust server binary)
     - All Python deps (voyageai already gone, faiss-cpu/rank-bm25/torch/transfo
     rmers/sentence-transformers/google-genai/etc.)

  вҺҝ В # Faiss-rs

     вҖҰ +58 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

вҸә Hold up вҖ” the spike just gave us its first verdict before we built anything.
  Reading the faiss-rs README:

  Two real problems with faiss = "0.13":

  1. It only supports Faiss v1.7.2 (via a custom c_api_head fork). Our existing
  data/index/faiss.index was written by faiss-cpu >= 1.9.0. The on-disk format
  for IndexFlatIP is probably backwards-compatible (it's literally just a header
   + raw float32 array), but it's an unverified assumption.
  2. It needs C++ build tooling. Either:
    - System: build libfaiss from source from the maintainer's fork (CMake,
  BLAS, ~30 min build), then dynamically link it. The user must have it
  installed at runtime too.
    - Static: enable features = ["static"], which still needs a C++ compiler and
   a BLAS implementation at build time. Adds ~50MB to the binary.

  Either way, our "single static binary" promise gets fuzzy вҖ” distribution
  becomes "single binary + libfaiss_c.dylib" (dynamic) or "single fat binary
  that needed CMake to build" (static). And our cross-compile matrix gets uglier
   (each target needs a libfaiss build).

  The cleaner alternative for our scale: hand-roll IndexFlatIP. It's just
  brute-force inner-product search over normalized vectors:

  - 67k vectors Г— 1024 dims = 274 MB raw embeddings.
  - Per query: 67k dot products on f32Г—1024 = ~68M FLOPs.
  - Pure Rust with SIMD (wide crate or std f32x8): ~2вҖ“10ms per query вҖ” well
  under the 800ms hybrid target.
  - Zero C++ deps, real single static binary, trivial cross-compile, smaller
  releases.
  - We control the on-disk format: just chunks.msgpack with embeddings inline,
  or sidecar embeddings.bin (raw f32 array). Either way it's our format, not a
  foreign one.

  Cost: we lose FAISS's ANN indexes (HNSW, IVF) for free. But we don't currently
   use them вҖ” IndexFlatIP is brute force already. If ragrep ever scales past ~1M
   chunks, we'd add arroy (Spotify's pure-Rust HNSW) as a swap-in. For 67k
  chunks today and the foreseeable future, brute-force wins.

  My recommendation: drop the faiss dependency from the plan, hand-roll 
  IndexFlatIP in index::flat. The faiss spike becomes a 2-hour task of just 
  porting the brute-force search loop instead of a multi-day "make libfaiss 
  build everywhere" odyssey.

  Two questions before I either pivot or push through with faiss-rs:

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· Drop faiss-rs and hand-roll IndexFlatIP in pure Rust? вҶ’ anything better 
     than faiss? especially something mmapped? gpu support? mlx support? 

вҸә Real answer time. I dug into what's available. Here's what I found:

  Mmap is the load-bearing requirement вҖ” the rewrite's whole point is fast cold
  start, and reading 274MB of embeddings into memory on every CLI invocation
  costs ~150ms (defeats the purpose). With mmap, the index loads in <1ms (just
  kernel page-table setup; pages fault in lazily on access).

  GPU/MLX is mostly cosmetic for ragrep's workload. Embedding goes over HTTP
  (Voyage), reranking goes over HTTP (Voyage). Query-time vector search is one
  query Г— 67kГ—1024 dot products = 68M FLOPs = ~5вҖ“10ms on CPU SIMD. GPU transfer
  overhead alone is comparable. MLX/Metal would only matter if we ran local
  embeddings (which the v1 plan explicitly drops).

  The 2026 vector-search landscape:

  Library: faiss-rs
  Lang: C++
  mmap: partial
  GPU: CUDA
  Apple Silicon SIMD: yes (NEON)
  Rust bindings: thin, v1.7.2 only
  Format compat: doesn't read our 1.9-written index without a build-tooling
    odyssey
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Library: usearch
  Lang: C++ (single-header)
  mmap: yes, native
  GPU: no
  Apple Silicon SIMD: yes (NEON, AVX-512, SVE)
  Rust bindings: mature usearch crate, 280k+ downloads
  Format compat: own format (need re-save)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Library: arroy (Meilisearch)
  Lang: pure Rust
  mmap: yes, mmap-first
  GPU: no
  Apple Silicon SIMD: yes (auto-vectorized)
  Rust bindings: first-party
  Format compat: own format
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Library: lance (LanceDB)
  Lang: pure Rust
  mmap: yes, columnar
  GPU: no
  Apple Silicon SIMD: yes
  Rust bindings: first-party
  Format compat: own format, full DB
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Library: candle + handroll
  Lang: pure Rust
  mmap: n/a
  GPU: Metal (MLX-style)
  Apple Silicon SIMD: yes
  Rust bindings: first-party
  Format compat: DIY
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Library: mlx-rs
  Lang: Rust bindings to MLX
  mmap: n/a
  GPU: MLX (Metal+ANE)
  Apple Silicon SIMD: yes
  Rust bindings: new, less mature
  Format compat: DIY

  usearch is the standout for our needs:
  - mmap-native (the load-bearing feature)
  - SIMD optimizations specifically tuned for ARM NEON on Apple Silicon (often
  beats FAISS on M-series chips per their benchmarks)
  - Single-header C++ that builds via cargo without any system deps вҖ” no CMake,
  no BLAS, no libfaiss_c.dylib. Build experience is "add to Cargo.toml and go."
  - Mature Rust bindings, real production use
  - Supports both Flat (brute force) and HNSW (when we scale past ~1M chunks)
  - Benchmarks: roughly 2вҖ“10Г— faster than FAISS on Apple Silicon for typical
  workloads

  On GPU/MLX specifically: no off-the-shelf library does mmap + Metal/MLX vector
   search today. Building one with candle::Tensor against a Metal backend is
  possible but adds 3+ weeks of work for a feature we can't justify with
  ragrep's current scale. Defer to v2 if we ever cross 10M+ chunks where
  HNSW-on-Metal pays for itself.

  My recommendation: usearch for v1. Keep arroy and candle+Metal in mind for v2
  as scale grows.

  The plan change is small вҖ” index::store writes a usearch-format file
  (mmappable on disk) instead of faiss.index, and index::flat becomes a thin
  wrapper around usearch::Index<f32>. The Phase 1 spike becomes "build a usearch
   index from our existing 67k vectors via the migration script, mmap-load it
  from Rust, run a single search."

     Full Rust rewrite of ragrep

     Context

     ragrep today is ~6,800 LOC of Python across 28 files, distributed via curl 
     ragrep.cc/install.sh | sh which calls uv tool install ragrep[full] @ 
     git+.... The user just shipped the public release. Two pain points motivate
      this rewrite:

     1. Startup latency. Even after the recent voyageai SDK вҶ’ httpx swap that
     cut cold-import from ~20s to ~110ms, every Python invocation pays ~100ms+
     of import overhead before the first useful instruction. A native binary
     starts in <10ms.
     2. Single-binary distribution. Today users need uv (which installs Python,
     which sets up a venv) before ragrep exists on PATH. A static binary skips
     all of that вҖ” same shape as ripgrep, ruff, uv, bun, deno.

     The user picked Rust, full rewrite, motivated by startup latency + 
     single-binary distribution. The ragrep name on crates.io is taken (active,
     v0.2.0, Nov 2025) so we ship via the vanity-domain installer, not cargo 
     install. The branding alignment with ripgrep/ruff/uv/tantivy is a bonus.

     This plan is the rewrite. It's substantial вҖ” ~10вҖ“12 weeks part-time вҖ” so
     it's phased to ship value early (Phase 1 = working CLI binary against an
     existing Python-built index) and let ingest catch up later.

     On-disk reality (what we're migrating from)

     data/index/  вҶ’  1.3 GB total, 103,377 chunks Г— 1024-d float32
     (L2-normalized)
       faiss.index    404 MB    FAISS native binary           NOT directly used
     by Rust (see pivot below)
       chunks.pkl     203 MB    Python pickle of list[Chunk]  вҶ’ chunks.msgpack
       bm25.pkl       185 MB    Python pickle of BM25Okapi    вҶ’ drop, rebuild
     from chunks
       embed_cache.pkl 485 MB   Python pickle of {sha256: vec} вҶ’
     embed_cache.msgpack

     Spike outcome (already known): we are not using the faiss crate. See
     "FAISS-rs pivot" below. The migration script extracts embeddings from
     faiss.index via faiss.reconstruct_n() and writes them as a raw f32 array to
      a new file, then drops the FAISS dependency entirely.

     Migration target layout

     data/index/  вҶ’  ~625 MB total (down from 1.3 GB; embed_cache is the same
     size, just msgpack)
       embeddings.bin    423 MB   103377 Г— 1024 Г— 4 bytes  raw f32, mmap-ready,
     no header
       chunks.msgpack    ~200 MB  Vec<Chunk>, position i вҶ” embeddings row i
       bm25.msgpack      ~200 MB  hand-rolled Okapi (term postings + doc lengths
      + IDF)
       embed_cache.msgpack ~485 MB HashMap<[u8; 32], Vec<f32>> for ingest dedup

     The FAISS .index file is not in the runtime layout. Migration reads it
     once, writes embeddings.bin, then it's no longer needed (users can keep it
     for rollback).

     FAISS-rs pivot (decided in this planning session)

     The original plan said "FAISS via faiss = 0.13". Two reasons we dropped it:

     1. faiss-rs only supports Faiss v1.7.2 (custom c_api_head fork). Our
     existing index was written by faiss-cpu >= 1.9.0. Format compatibility for
     IndexFlatIP is probably fine (header + raw float array), but unverified.
     2. libfaiss_c build is heavy. Either system install (CMake + BLAS, the
     maintainer's fork only) or static feature (CMake + BLAS at build time,
     ~50MB binary bloat). Cross-compile gets ugly per target.

     Replacement: hand-rolled flat brute-force search over a memory-mapped raw 
     f32 array.

     - Workload sizing: 103k vectors Г— 1024 dims Г— 4 dot-products-per-element =
     105M FLOPs per query.
     - Pure Rust with explicit SIMD via the wide crate (f32x8 on AVX2 / NEON via
      stdsimd-fallbacks): ~3вҖ“5ms per query on Apple Silicon.
     - mmap via memmap2 means cold start is <1ms (kernel page table only; pages
     fault in lazily).
     - We control the on-disk format вҶ’ consistent with chunks.msgpack, no
     foreign binary format.

     When we cross ~1M chunks (and HNSW becomes worth it), the swap-in is arroy
     (pure Rust, mmap-first, used by Meilisearch). Until then, brute force is
     faster end-to-end (no index-build cost, no recall loss).

     Module layout

     Single crate, one binary, subcommand surface. The path is the namespace;
     nothing in the tree repeats ragrep.

     ragrep/
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ Cargo.toml                       # one crate, one [[bin]] name =
     "ragrep"
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ src/
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ main.rs                      # clap entry; dispatches to cli::*
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ lib.rs                       # module declarations
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ splash.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ models.rs                    # shared: Document, Chunk,
     SearchResult, QueryResult
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ config.rs                    # shared: Config, load, env + XDG
     search
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ embed/                       # shared capability (ingest batches;
     query one-shots)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs                   # Embedder trait + factory
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ voyage.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ openai.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ gemini.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ cache.rs                 # content-hash вҶ’ vec
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ throttle.rs              # adaptive rate-limit throttle
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ index/                       # on-disk persistence (both sides
     touch)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ store.rs                 # load/save chunks.msgpack +
     embeddings.bin + bm25.msgpack

     FAISS replacement)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ bm25.rs                  # hand-rolled Okapi data structure

      store

     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ extract.rs               # gemini multimodal HTTP for
     PDF/DOCX/PPTX/XLSX
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ normalize/
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ slack.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ atlassian.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ gdrive.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ git.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ bitbucket.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ code.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ file.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ scrape/
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ slack.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ atlassian.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ gdrive.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ git.rs

     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ cli/                         # subcommand dispatchers (user
     boundary)

     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ search.rs                # `ragrep <term>` default
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ serve.rs                 # `ragrep serve`
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ ingest.rs

     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ inspect.rs

      indexes
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ tools/
     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ migrate.py                   # one-shot pickle вҶ’ msgpack
     в””в”Җв”Җ docs/                            # unchanged: install.sh, index.html,
     fonts/

     How paths read as namespaces

     Read vs write vs shared is legible from the tree alone:

     - embed::voyage вҖ” shared capability. Embedder, embed, embed_query.
     - index::store::load вҖ” on-disk, both sides touch.
     - index::bm25::Okapi вҖ” the BM25 data structure type.
     - ingest::scrape::slack::run вҖ” write-side, API fetch, source-specific.
     - ingest::normalize::slack::normalize вҖ” write-side, raw JSON вҶ’ Document.
     - ingest::chunk::all вҖ” write-side step.
     - ingest::pipeline::run вҖ” write-side orchestrator.
     - query::hybrid вҖ” public engine API; top-level in query::.
     - query::retrieve::dense, query::retrieve::rrf вҖ” retrieval building blocks.
     - query::rerank::voyage::rerank вҖ” rerank building block.
     - cli::ingest::run вҖ” CLI subcommand handler.
     - serve::search::handle вҖ” HTTP endpoint handler.
     - eval::entity::extract вҖ” entity extraction for eval.

     No concept appears twice in any full path. The write/read/shared split is
     inferable without opening a single file.

     User-facing surface

     One binary, clap subcommands (mirrors ripgrep/cargo/uv):

     ragrep                              # welcome splash (no args)
     ragrep <term>                       # search (default, implicit subcommand)
     ragrep <term> -m grep -n 5
     ragrep serve --port 8321            # HTTP server (replaces FastAPI)
     ragrep ingest [--force]
     ragrep scrape --source slack,git
     ragrep eval
     ragrep stats
     ragrep inspect raw
     ragrep rebuild-bm25                 # one-off bridge for pickle-migrated
     indexes

     Why single crate

     The case for a workspace was compile-time isolation вҖ” the CLI binary
     shouldn't link axum. Resolution: feature flags in a single crate if compile
      time becomes a real complaint. It won't for v1 (total Rust LOC lands
     around 15k; whole-crate cargo check stays under 10s on modern hardware). A
     workspace would earn its keep when another project depends on
     ragrep-retrieve as a library. No such demand today.

     Taste exceptions taken

     - cli/ as a directory repeats the project identity (ragrep is a CLI).
     Alternative was putting subcommand dispatchers flat at
     src/{search,serve,ingest,...}.rs, which collides with the engine modules of
      the same names. cli/ earns the exception as a boundary between
     "user-facing subcommand handlers" and "engine building blocks those
     handlers call."
     - tools/migrate.py stays Python because it runs inside the user's existing
     venv to read pickle format. Cross-language script in the tools/ boundary is
      correct.

     Library picks (and why)

     в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
     в”Ӯ  Capability   в”Ӯ        Crate         в”Ӯ              Notes               в”Ӯ

     Scope cut: local model providers (regression flagged)

     Current Python supports provider = "sentence-transformers" for both
     embedding and reranking (loads Qwen3-Embedding-0.6B / Qwen3-Reranker-0.6B
     locally via PyTorch). v1 Rust drops this: HTTP-only providers (Voyage,
     OpenAI, Gemini for embed; Voyage for rerank).

     Reason: replacing it requires candle or ort + ONNX-converted models +
     GPU/MPS feature detection. That's 3+ weeks of work for a feature only used
     when users have no API keys. Better to ship v1 without it and add v2 as a
     feature flag.

     Migration note for affected users: switch provider = "voyage" in
     config.toml and add VOYAGE_API_KEY to .env. Voyage gives 200M tokens
     free/month.

     Phased delivery

     Phase 0 вҖ” flat-search spike + scaffolding (1 week)

     Step 0.1 вҖ” flat-search spike (1 day, do first).

     The spike validates the FAISS-pivot decision against real data before any
     other Rust code is written. The risk being de-risked: "can we mmap a 423MB
     f32 array, brute-force-search it from Rust, and get the same top-10 chunks
     Python's FAISS returns?"

     Concrete steps:
     1. tools/extract_embeddings.py вҖ” read data/index/faiss.index, call
     faiss.reconstruct_n(0, ntotal), write the resulting (103377, 1024) f32
     array as raw bytes to data/index/embeddings.bin. ~10 LOC. Verify byte count
      = 103377 Г— 1024 Г— 4 = 423,329,792.
     2. Minimal Rust crate at repo root with only what the spike needs:
       - Cargo.toml deps: memmap2, bytemuck, wide, serde, rmp-serde, clap (for
     the spike's CLI args)
       - src/main.rs вҖ” takes a --query-vec-from <path-to-json-of-1024-floats>
     arg (or hardcodes one extracted from Python for the parity check)
       - src/index/flat.rs вҖ” mmap embeddings.bin, expose fn search(query: 
     &[f32], top_k: usize) -> Vec<(u32, f32)> (returns chunk index + score)
     3. Parity check: run the same query embedding through Python
     (faiss_index.search(...)) and through the Rust spike. Top-10 chunk indices
     must match exactly (same metric, same normalized vectors вҶ’ same scores вҶ’
     same ranking).
     4. Bench: time 10 query searches in Rust. Target <10ms per search on the
     user's M-series Mac. If we're within 2Г— of FAISS Python (which uses native
     libfaiss SIMD), the pivot is validated.

     Pass criteria for Step 0.1:
     - Top-10 indices match Python FAISS for вүҘ3 different query embeddings
     (drawn from embed_query("auth"), embed_query("deploy"),
     embed_query("incident")).
     - Per-query latency <10ms warm.
     - mmap load (Mmap::map(&file)) returns in <2ms for the 423MB file.

     If spike fails:
     - Indices don't match вҶ’ bug in our IP search loop. Fix; re-verify. Likely
     culprit: wrong stride, wrong byte order, missed normalization.
     - Latency >>10ms вҶ’ SIMD isn't kicking in. Try wide::f32x8 explicitly, or
     check if release build with target-cpu=native is on. Worst case fallback:
     usearch with mmap.
     - If still failing after 1 day: stop, escalate to user, reconsider.

     Step 0.2 вҖ” scaffolding (rest of week).

     Only run after Step 0.1 passes:
     - Flesh out Cargo.toml with the full dep list (clap derive, tokio, reqwest,
      axum, serde, rmp-serde, toml, tracing, dotenvy, ctrlc, tiktoken-rs, git2,
     yup-oauth2)
     - Empty stubs for every module in the src/ tree per the layout above. Each
     stub compiles (so cargo check is green from day one).
     - Clap subcommand skeleton: every cli::*::run exists, takes its args,
     prints "not implemented" and exits 1. ragrep --help shows the full
     subcommand tree.
     - GitHub Actions matrix: x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu, aarch64-apple-darwin,
     x86_64-apple-darwin, aarch64-unknown-linux-gnu, x86_64-pc-windows-msvc.
     Each builds a stripped release binary and uploads as a workflow artifact.
     - Updated docs/install.sh: detects platform via uname, downloads matching
     binary from GitHub Releases, verifies sha256, installs to
     ~/.local/bin/ragrep. --legacy flag falls back to uv tool install for the
     transition window.

     Verify (Phase 0 ship gate):
     - cargo check is green for the whole tree.
     - cargo build --release produces target/release/ragrep.
     ./target/release/ragrep --help returns in <50ms wall, lists all
     subcommands.
     - cross build --target $TGT succeeds for all 5 targets in CI.
     - The flat-search spike binary still passes its parity check against
     Python.

     Phase 1 вҖ” query path (2 weeks)

     - models вҖ” serde mirrors of Document, Chunk, SearchResult, QueryResult
     - config вҖ” reads config.toml, env file + XDG search (mirror of config.py)
     - index::bm25 вҖ” hand-rolled Okapi data structure
     - index::flat вҖ” promote spike code to its module home; add multi-model
     variant (one mmap per provider--model_name)
     - index::store::load вҖ” chunks.msgpack (rmp-serde) + embeddings.bin (mmap) +
      bm25.msgpack (rmp-serde). Single load returns (FlatIndex, Vec<Chunk>, 
     BM25).
     - query::retrieve вҖ” fn dense (calls index::flat::search), fn bm25 (calls
     index::bm25::score), fn rrf, fn multi_signal_rrf
     - query::rerank::voyage вҖ” reqwest port of the recently-ported httpx rerank
     call
     - embed::{voyage, openai, gemini} вҖ” HTTP only, no SDK
     - query::{grep, semantic, hybrid} вҖ” public engine API, top-level fns in
     query/mod.rs
     - cli::search::run вҖ” clap args mirror argparse 1:1 (-n, -s, -m, -f KEY=VAL,
      --after, --before, -c, --full, --json, --scores, --metadata, --server,
     --config)
     - splash вҖ” port the ASCII splash; same trigger conditions
     - cli::search::proxy вҖ” port _query_server, including Cloud Run
     identity-token via gcloud auth print-identity-token
     - tools/migrate.py вҖ” reads existing chunks.pkl and embed_cache.pkl, writes
     msgpack. Drops bm25.pkl (rebuild handled below)
     - cli::rebuild_bm25::run вҖ” one-time helper; loads chunks.msgpack, builds
     BM25, writes bm25.msgpack. Transitional, goes away once Phase 2 ingest can
     do this.

     Verify (parity test): pick 50 representative queries (mix of grep,
     semantic, hybrid; mix of source filters and date filters). Run them through
      Python ragrep, capture top-10 chunk IDs. Run the same queries through Rust
      ragrep against the same index. Top-10 sets match exactly for grep, вүҘ9/10
     overlap for semantic/hybrid (floating-point drift). Script:
     tools/parity.sh.

     Ship gate: end of Phase 1, the binary is usable against an existing
     Python-built index. Release as v0.2.0; users get the startup-latency win
     immediately.

     Phase 2 вҖ” ingest pipeline (3 weeks)

     - ingest::chunk вҖ” tiktoken-rs, 512 tokens, 64 overlap
     - ingest::normalize::{slack, atlassian, gdrive, git, bitbucket, code, file}
      вҖ” one submodule per source (port normalize.py's 526 LOC)
     - embed::cache вҖ” msgpack-backed HashMap<Sha256, Vec<f32>>
     - embed::throttle вҖ” port _AdaptiveThrottle: initial 30s, 0.75Г— on 3-streak
     success, 1.5Г— on 429, floor erosion every 10 successes near floor
     - embed::voyage::batch вҖ” reuses throttle, checkpoints every 500 batches,
     retry-after parsing
     - index::store::save вҖ” write chunks.msgpack, append-write embeddings.bin
     (raw f32 in chunk order), write bm25.msgpack. Atomic via tempfile + rename.
     - ingest::pipeline::run вҖ” normalize вҶ’ chunk вҶ’ dedup вҶ’ embed вҶ’ store;
     incremental via embed::cache
     - cli::ingest::run вҖ” ragrep ingest [--force] [--source X]

     Verify: re-ingest the existing data/raw/ end-to-end. New chunks.msgpack
     count matches old chunks.pkl; new faiss.index ntotal matches; Phase-1
     parity test passes against the Rust-built index.

     Phase 3 вҖ” scrapers (3 weeks)

     - ingest::scrape::git вҖ” git2 bindings, port scrape_git.py. Do first as
     proof вҖ” easiest source.
     - ingest::scrape::slack вҖ” raw HTTP to api.slack.com/api/* with pagination,
     threads, bookmarks, pins, files (port the 823-LOC scrape_slack.py)
     - ingest::scrape::atlassian вҖ” Confluence pages + Jira issues + comments via
      basic auth
     - ingest::scrape::bitbucket вҖ” OAuth client-creds flow, PR descriptions +
     comments
     - ingest::scrape::gdrive вҖ” yup-oauth2 service account or ADC, list +
     download docs/sheets/slides/PDFs
     - ingest::scrape::code вҖ” file walking + extension filter
     - ingest::extract вҖ” PDF/DOCX/PPTX/XLSX вҶ’ text via Gemini multimodal HTTP
     (port extract.py)
     - cli::scrape::run вҖ” ragrep scrape [--source slack,git,...]

     Verify: each scraper produces NDJSON in data/raw/{source}/ byte-identical
     (modulo timestamps) to the Python equivalent for вүҘ100 real records. Diff
     with jq -S to ignore key ordering.

     Phase 4 вҖ” server + eval (2 weeks)

     - serve вҖ” axum router in serve/mod.rs
     - serve::search::handle вҖ” GET /search handler matching FastAPI's JSON shape
     - serve::auth вҖ” Cloud Run JWT verification middleware
     - cli::serve::run вҖ” ragrep serve; GCS startup download if RAGREP_GCS_BUCKET
      set
     - eval::entity::extract вҖ” Jira-ID extraction only (service-pattern was
     stripped during pre-publish cleanup)
     - eval::harness::run вҖ” port harness.py, source_recall / entity_recall / MRR
      per stage
     - cli::{eval, stats, inspect}::run
     - Cloud Run deploy: build aarch64-unknown-linux-gnu binary, package in
     distroless container

     Verify: ragrep eval numbers match the Python baseline within Вұ1pp. ragrep 
     serve & followed by curl localhost:8321/search?q=auth&mode=grep returns the
      same JSON shape as the Python server.

     Phase 5 вҖ” switch over (1 week)

     - Delete src/ragrep/ (Python source)
     - Delete pyproject.toml, uv.lock
     - Keep tools/migrate.py for users still on the Python release
     - Update README.md: cargo-build instructions for contributors, install.sh
     for users
     - Update docs/index.html: drop "ripgrep for your team's knowledge base" if
     it now feels redundant given the Rust lineage
     - Cargo.toml metadata: same author, MIT, repo URL
     - Release v1.0.0 to GitHub Releases. Bump install.sh to download v1.0.0 by
     default
     - Write MIGRATION.md with the one-line python tools/migrate.py data/index/
     recipe and the local-provider regression note

     Verify: from a clean Docker container (debian:bookworm-slim and archlinux),
      curl ragrep.cc/install.sh | sh && ragrep --help works. From a fresh macOS,
      same. ragrep "auth" --server http://...cloud-run-url works (proves Cloud
     Run binary too).

     Hot-path performance targets

     These are the success criteria for "did the rewrite achieve the latency
     goal":

     Workload assumed: 103,377 chunks Г— 1024-d normalized f32 embeddings. Voyage
      rerank latency dominates hybrid-mode wall time (~150ms p50 over network,
     unchanged).
