  What ships in v0.2.0-rust: ragrep <term> works in all 3 modes (grep, semantic,
   hybrid) against either a local migrated index or a remote ragrep serve
  deployment. The migration is a one-time python tools/migrate.py data/index/
  recipe that drops in alongside the existing Python install.

  Phase 1 wrap commits on rust branch:
  - f50d48e вҖ” grep mode end-to-end
  - 1213078 вҖ” semantic + hybrid + rerank
  - 5d8531c вҖ” pre-warm rayon + 30-query parity
  - 2fadf45 вҖ” server-mode proxy

  CI is queued for the latest push. Pre-warmed rayon is in (cold-call hides
  behind config + msgpack load now). Server proxy intentionally has no Cloud Run
   auth вҖ” that's deployment-side, not CLI-side.

  What Phase 1 doesn't have yet (intentionally deferred to later phases):
  - --filter, --after, --before (CLI bails today). Cheap to add вҖ” port
  parse_filters and parse_date from search.py into query::filters and apply in
  grep/semantic/hybrid. ~half day.
  - Multi-model embeddings (the models = [...] config knob).
  - cli::stats, cli::inspect, cli::eval (Phase 4 territory).

  Want me to bang out the filter/date support next (small, finishes Phase 1's
  user-facing surface), or jump to Phase 2 (the ingest pipeline вҖ” chunking,
  normalize per source, full embed batching with throttle)?

вҸә Two scope questions before exiting plan mode:

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· Which Phase 2 features should ship in v1 vs defer? вҶ’ lets allow embedding
      services to be provider/model agnostic
     В· Embed cache format: keep msgpack (1.1GB current) or switch to compact 
     binary? вҶ’ is the compact .bin format taknig a r/w speed hit? 

вҸә Two big answers:

  1. Provider/model agnostic embedding. Restructure into a trait so
  Voyage/OpenAI/Gemini are interchangeable (and cache is per-model). Bigger v1
  scope but right architecture.

  2. Binary cache format speed: It's actually faster, not slower. msgpack:
  1.1GB, ~5s load (allocate Vec per entry). Binary: 500MB, ~2s load (mmap +
  bytemuck cast вҖ” zero decode cost). I had the recommendation backwards.
  Switching to binary.

  вҺҝ В Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/melodic-spinning-simon.md В· /plan to edit
     Full Rust rewrite of ragrep

     Context

     ragrep today is ~6,800 LOC of Python across 28 files, distributed via curl 
     ragrep.cc/install.sh | sh which calls uv tool install ragrep[full] @ 
     git+.... The user just shipped the public release. Two pain points motivate
      this rewrite:

     1. Startup latency. Even after the recent voyageai SDK вҶ’ httpx swap that
     cut cold-import from ~20s to ~110ms, every Python invocation pays ~100ms+
     of import overhead before the first useful instruction. A native binary
     starts in <10ms.
     2. Single-binary distribution. Today users need uv (which installs Python,
     which sets up a venv) before ragrep exists on PATH. A static binary skips
     all of that вҖ” same shape as ripgrep, ruff, uv, bun, deno.

     The user picked Rust, full rewrite, motivated by startup latency + 
     single-binary distribution. The ragrep name on crates.io is taken (active,
     v0.2.0, Nov 2025) so we ship via the vanity-domain installer, not cargo 
     install. The branding alignment with ripgrep/ruff/uv/tantivy is a bonus.

     This plan is the rewrite. It's substantial вҖ” ~10вҖ“12 weeks part-time вҖ” so
     it's phased to ship value early (Phase 1 = working CLI binary against an
     existing Python-built index) and let ingest catch up later.

     On-disk reality (what we're migrating from)

     data/index/  вҶ’  1.3 GB total, 103,377 chunks Г— 1024-d float32
     (L2-normalized)
       faiss.index    404 MB    FAISS native binary           NOT directly used
     by Rust (see pivot below)
       chunks.pkl     203 MB    Python pickle of list[Chunk]  вҶ’ chunks.msgpack
       bm25.pkl       185 MB    Python pickle of BM25Okapi    вҶ’ drop, rebuild
     from chunks
       embed_cache.pkl 485 MB   Python pickle of {sha256: vec} вҶ’
     embed_cache.msgpack

     Spike outcome (already known): we are not using the faiss crate. See
     "FAISS-rs pivot" below. The migration script extracts embeddings from
     faiss.index via faiss.reconstruct_n() and writes them as a raw f32 array to
      a new file, then drops the FAISS dependency entirely.

     Migration target layout

     data/index/  вҶ’  ~625 MB total (down from 1.3 GB; embed_cache is the same
     size, just msgpack)
       embeddings.bin    423 MB   103377 Г— 1024 Г— 4 bytes  raw f32, mmap-ready,
     no header
       chunks.msgpack    ~200 MB  Vec<Chunk>, position i вҶ” embeddings row i
       bm25.msgpack      ~200 MB  hand-rolled Okapi (term postings + doc lengths
      + IDF)
       embed_cache.msgpack ~485 MB HashMap<[u8; 32], Vec<f32>> for ingest dedup

     The FAISS .index file is not in the runtime layout. Migration reads it
     once, writes embeddings.bin, then it's no longer needed (users can keep it
     for rollback).

     FAISS-rs pivot (decided in this planning session)

     The original plan said "FAISS via faiss = 0.13". Two reasons we dropped it:

     1. faiss-rs only supports Faiss v1.7.2 (custom c_api_head fork). Our
     existing index was written by faiss-cpu >= 1.9.0. Format compatibility for
     IndexFlatIP is probably fine (header + raw float array), but unverified.
     2. libfaiss_c build is heavy. Either system install (CMake + BLAS, the
     maintainer's fork only) or static feature (CMake + BLAS at build time,
     ~50MB binary bloat). Cross-compile gets ugly per target.

     Replacement: hand-rolled flat brute-force search over a memory-mapped raw 
     f32 array.

     - Workload sizing: 103k vectors Г— 1024 dims Г— 4 dot-products-per-element =
     105M FLOPs per query.
     - Pure Rust with explicit SIMD via the wide crate (f32x8 on AVX2 / NEON via
      stdsimd-fallbacks): ~3вҖ“5ms per query on Apple Silicon.
     - mmap via memmap2 means cold start is <1ms (kernel page table only; pages
     fault in lazily).
     - We control the on-disk format вҶ’ consistent with chunks.msgpack, no
     foreign binary format.

     When we cross ~1M chunks (and HNSW becomes worth it), the swap-in is arroy
     (pure Rust, mmap-first, used by Meilisearch). Until then, brute force is
     faster end-to-end (no index-build cost, no recall loss).

     Module layout

     Single crate, one binary, subcommand surface. The path is the namespace;
     nothing in the tree repeats ragrep.

     ragrep/
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ Cargo.toml                       # one crate, one [[bin]] name =
     "ragrep"
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ src/
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ main.rs                      # clap entry; dispatches to cli::*
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ lib.rs                       # module declarations
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ splash.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ models.rs                    # shared: Document, Chunk,
     SearchResult, QueryResult
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ config.rs                    # shared: Config, load, env + XDG
     search
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ embed/                       # shared capability (ingest batches;
     query one-shots)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs                   # Embedder trait + factory
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ voyage.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ openai.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ gemini.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ cache.rs                 # content-hash вҶ’ vec
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ throttle.rs              # adaptive rate-limit throttle
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ index/                       # on-disk persistence (both sides
     touch)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ store.rs                 # load/save chunks.msgpack +
     embeddings.bin + bm25.msgpack
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ flat.rs                  # mmapped brute-force IP search (the
     FAISS replacement)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ bm25.rs                  # hand-rolled Okapi data structure
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ingest/                      # write side
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ pipeline.rs              # scrape вҶ’ normalize вҶ’ chunk вҶ’ embed вҶ’
      store
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ chunk.rs                 # 512-token chunking
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ extract.rs               # gemini multimodal HTTP for
     PDF/DOCX/PPTX/XLSX
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ normalize/
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ slack.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ atlassian.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ gdrive.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ git.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ bitbucket.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ code.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ file.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ scrape/
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ slack.rs
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ atlassian.rs

     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ harness.rs               # source_recall, entity_recall, MRR
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ serve/                       # HTTP server (backs `ragrep serve`)
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs                   # axum router
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ auth.rs                  # Cloud Run JWT middleware
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ search.rs                # GET /search handler
     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ cli/                         # subcommand dispatchers (user
     boundary)
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs                   # Subcommand enum + dispatch
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ search.rs                # `ragrep <term>` default
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ serve.rs                 # `ragrep serve`
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ ingest.rs
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ scrape.rs
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ eval.rs
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ stats.rs
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ inspect.rs
     в”Ӯ       в””в”Җв”Җ rebuild_bm25.rs          # transient bridge for pickle-migrated
      indexes
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ tools/
     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ migrate.py                   # one-shot pickle вҶ’ msgpack
     в””в”Җв”Җ docs/                            # unchanged: install.sh, index.html,
     fonts/

     How paths read as namespaces

     Read vs write vs shared is legible from the tree alone:

     - embed::voyage вҖ” shared capability. Embedder, embed, embed_query.
     - index::store::load вҖ” on-disk, both sides touch.
     - index::bm25::Okapi вҖ” the BM25 data structure type.
     - ingest::scrape::slack::run вҖ” write-side, API fetch, source-specific.
     - ingest::normalize::slack::normalize вҖ” write-side, raw JSON вҶ’ Document.
     - ingest::chunk::all вҖ” write-side step.
     - ingest::pipeline::run вҖ” write-side orchestrator.
     - query::hybrid вҖ” public engine API; top-level in query::.
     - query::retrieve::dense, query::retrieve::rrf вҖ” retrieval building blocks.
     - query::rerank::voyage::rerank вҖ” rerank building block.
     - cli::ingest::run вҖ” CLI subcommand handler.
     - serve::search::handle вҖ” HTTP endpoint handler.
     - eval::entity::extract вҖ” entity extraction for eval.

     No concept appears twice in any full path. The write/read/shared split is
     inferable without opening a single file.

     User-facing surface

     One binary, clap subcommands (mirrors ripgrep/cargo/uv):

     ragrep                              # welcome splash (no args)
     ragrep <term>                       # search (default, implicit subcommand)
     ragrep <term> -m grep -n 5
     ragrep serve --port 8321            # HTTP server (replaces FastAPI)
     ragrep ingest [--force]
     ragrep scrape --source slack,git
     ragrep eval
     ragrep stats
     ragrep inspect raw
     ragrep rebuild-bm25                 # one-off bridge for pickle-migrated
     indexes

     Why single crate

     The case for a workspace was compile-time isolation вҖ” the CLI binary
     shouldn't link axum. Resolution: feature flags in a single crate if compile
      time becomes a real complaint. It won't for v1 (total Rust LOC lands
     around 15k; whole-crate cargo check stays under 10s on modern hardware). A
     workspace would earn its keep when another project depends on
     ragrep-retrieve as a library. No such demand today.

     Taste exceptions taken

     - cli/ as a directory repeats the project identity (ragrep is a CLI).
     Alternative was putting subcommand dispatchers flat at
     src/{search,serve,ingest,...}.rs, which collides with the engine modules of
      the same names. cli/ earns the exception as a boundary between
     "user-facing subcommand handlers" and "engine building blocks those
     handlers call."
     - tools/migrate.py stays Python because it runs inside the user's existing
     venv to read pickle format. Cross-language script in the tools/ boundary is
      correct.

     Library picks (and why)

     в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
     в”Ӯ  Capability   в”Ӯ        Crate         в”Ӯ              Notes               в”Ӯ

     Scope cut: local model providers (regression flagged)

     Current Python supports provider = "sentence-transformers" for both
     embedding and reranking (loads Qwen3-Embedding-0.6B / Qwen3-Reranker-0.6B
     locally via PyTorch). v1 Rust drops this: HTTP-only providers (Voyage,
     OpenAI, Gemini for embed; Voyage for rerank).

     Reason: replacing it requires candle or ort + ONNX-converted models +
     GPU/MPS feature detection. That's 3+ weeks of work for a feature only used
     when users have no API keys. Better to ship v1 without it and add v2 as a
     feature flag.

     Migration note for affected users: switch provider = "voyage" in
     config.toml and add VOYAGE_API_KEY to .env. Voyage gives 200M tokens
     free/month.

     Phased delivery

     Phase 0 вҖ” flat-search spike + scaffolding (1 week)

     Step 0.1 вҖ” flat-search spike (1 day, do first).

     The spike validates the FAISS-pivot decision against real data before any
     other Rust code is written. The risk being de-risked: "can we mmap a 423MB
     f32 array, brute-force-search it from Rust, and get the same top-10 chunks
     Python's FAISS returns?"

     Concrete steps:
     1. tools/extract_embeddings.py вҖ” read data/index/faiss.index, call
     faiss.reconstruct_n(0, ntotal), write the resulting (103377, 1024) f32
     array as raw bytes to data/index/embeddings.bin. ~10 LOC. Verify byte count
      = 103377 Г— 1024 Г— 4 = 423,329,792.
     2. Minimal Rust crate at repo root with only what the spike needs:
       - Cargo.toml deps: memmap2, bytemuck, wide, serde, rmp-serde, clap (for
     the spike's CLI args)
       - src/main.rs вҖ” takes a --query-vec-from <path-to-json-of-1024-floats>
     arg (or hardcodes one extracted from Python for the parity check)
       - src/index/flat.rs вҖ” mmap embeddings.bin, expose fn search(query: 
     &[f32], top_k: usize) -> Vec<(u32, f32)> (returns chunk index + score)
     3. Parity check: run the same query embedding through Python
     (faiss_index.search(...)) and through the Rust spike. Top-10 chunk indices
     must match exactly (same metric, same normalized vectors вҶ’ same scores вҶ’
     same ranking).
     4. Bench: time 10 query searches in Rust. Target <10ms per search on the
     user's M-series Mac. If we're within 2Г— of FAISS Python (which uses native
     libfaiss SIMD), the pivot is validated.

     Pass criteria for Step 0.1:
     - Top-10 indices match Python FAISS for вүҘ3 different query embeddings
     (drawn from embed_query("auth"), embed_query("deploy"),
     embed_query("incident")).
     - Per-query latency <10ms warm.
     - mmap load (Mmap::map(&file)) returns in <2ms for the 423MB file.

     If spike fails:
     - Indices don't match вҶ’ bug in our IP search loop. Fix; re-verify. Likely
     culprit: wrong stride, wrong byte order, missed normalization.
     - Latency >>10ms вҶ’ SIMD isn't kicking in. Try wide::f32x8 explicitly, or
     check if release build with target-cpu=native is on. Worst case fallback:
     usearch with mmap.
     - If still failing after 1 day: stop, escalate to user, reconsider.

     Step 0.2 вҖ” scaffolding (rest of week).

     Only run after Step 0.1 passes:
     - Flesh out Cargo.toml with the full dep list (clap derive, tokio, reqwest,
      axum, serde, rmp-serde, toml, tracing, dotenvy, ctrlc, tiktoken-rs, git2,
     yup-oauth2)
     - Empty stubs for every module in the src/ tree per the layout above. Each
     stub compiles (so cargo check is green from day one).
     - Clap subcommand skeleton: every cli::*::run exists, takes its args,
     prints "not implemented" and exits 1. ragrep --help shows the full
     subcommand tree.
     - GitHub Actions matrix: x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu, aarch64-apple-darwin,
     x86_64-apple-darwin, aarch64-unknown-linux-gnu, x86_64-pc-windows-msvc.
     Each builds a stripped release binary and uploads as a workflow artifact.
     - Updated docs/install.sh: detects platform via uname, downloads matching
     binary from GitHub Releases, verifies sha256, installs to
     ~/.local/bin/ragrep. --legacy flag falls back to uv tool install for the
     transition window.

     Verify (Phase 0 ship gate):
     - cargo check is green for the whole tree.
     - cargo build --release produces target/release/ragrep.
     ./target/release/ragrep --help returns in <50ms wall, lists all
     subcommands.
     - cross build --target $TGT succeeds for all 5 targets in CI.
     - The flat-search spike binary still passes its parity check against
     Python.

     Phase 1 вҖ” query path (2 weeks)

     - models вҖ” serde mirrors of Document, Chunk, SearchResult, QueryResult
     - config вҖ” reads config.toml, env file + XDG search (mirror of config.py)
     - index::bm25 вҖ” hand-rolled Okapi data structure
     - index::flat вҖ” promote spike code to its module home; add multi-model
     variant (one mmap per provider--model_name)
     - index::store::load вҖ” chunks.msgpack (rmp-serde) + embeddings.bin (mmap) +
      bm25.msgpack (rmp-serde). Single load returns (FlatIndex, Vec<Chunk>, 
     BM25).
     - query::retrieve вҖ” fn dense (calls index::flat::search), fn bm25 (calls
     index::bm25::score), fn rrf, fn multi_signal_rrf
     - query::rerank::voyage вҖ” reqwest port of the recently-ported httpx rerank
     call
     - embed::{voyage, openai, gemini} вҖ” HTTP only, no SDK
     - query::{grep, semantic, hybrid} вҖ” public engine API, top-level fns in
     query/mod.rs
     - cli::search::run вҖ” clap args mirror argparse 1:1 (-n, -s, -m, -f KEY=VAL,
      --after, --before, -c, --full, --json, --scores, --metadata, --server,
     --config)
     - splash вҖ” port the ASCII splash; same trigger conditions
     - cli::search::proxy вҖ” port _query_server, including Cloud Run
     identity-token via gcloud auth print-identity-token
     - tools/migrate.py вҖ” reads existing chunks.pkl and embed_cache.pkl, writes
     msgpack. Drops bm25.pkl (rebuild handled below)
     - cli::rebuild_bm25::run вҖ” one-time helper; loads chunks.msgpack, builds
     BM25, writes bm25.msgpack. Transitional, goes away once Phase 2 ingest can
     do this.

     Verify (parity test): pick 50 representative queries (mix of grep,
     semantic, hybrid; mix of source filters and date filters). Run them through
      Python ragrep, capture top-10 chunk IDs. Run the same queries through Rust
      ragrep against the same index. Top-10 sets match exactly for grep, вүҘ9/10
     overlap for semantic/hybrid (floating-point drift). Script:
     tools/parity.sh.

     Ship gate: end of Phase 1, the binary is usable against an existing
     Python-built index. Release as v0.2.0; users get the startup-latency win
     immediately.

     Phase 2 вҖ” ingest pipeline (3 weeks, the write side)

     Phase 1 shipped the read side (search modes + filters + server proxy +
     30/30 parity).
     Phase 2 closes the loop by porting the Python ingest pipeline so a deployed
      Rust
     binary can scrape вҶ’ normalize вҶ’ chunk вҶ’ embed вҶ’ store from scratch.

     What Phase 1 already left in place that Phase 2 builds on:
       models, config, index::flat (mmap read), index::bm25 (build + save),
       index::store::{save_chunks, save_bm25} (atomic write done), embed::voyage
       (sync HTTP one-shot port), query::filters, cli::run dispatch.

     Missing pieces (in build order):
       embed::Embedder      trait + factory; 3 provider impls (voyage / openai /
      gemini)
       embed::cache         binary embed_cache/{provider}--{model}.bin,
     mmap-friendly
       embed::throttle      port _AdaptiveThrottle from embed.py:39
       embed::voyage::batch (+ openai::batch, gemini::batch) вҖ” sync HTTP,
     retry/backoff
       ingest::chunk        port chunk.py (no real tokenizer; see Tokenization
     note)
       ingest::normalize/*  9 source-specific modules, port normalize.py (526
     LOC)
       ingest::pipeline     orchestrator, mirrors pipeline.py::ingest
       cli::ingest::run     ragrep ingest [--force] [--source X]

     Step 2.1a вҖ” embed::Embedder trait + factory (~ВҪ day)

     Design the embedding layer so providers and models are swappable. The
     pipeline
     holds a Box<dyn Embedder> and never knows whether it's talking to Voyage,
     OpenAI, or Gemini. cli::ingest::run reads cfg.embedding.{provider, 
     model_name}
     and calls the factory.

     // embed/mod.rs
     pub trait Embedder: Send + Sync {
         fn provider(&self) -> &str;
         fn model(&self) -> &str;
         fn dim(&self) -> usize;
         fn embed_query(&self, text: &str) -> Result<Vec<f32>>;
         fn embed_documents(
             &self,
             texts: &[&str],
             batch_size: usize,
             checkpoint: Option<&Path>,
         ) -> Result<Vec<Vec<f32>>>;
     }

     pub fn make(provider: &str, model: &str) -> Result<Box<dyn Embedder>> { ...
      }

     Phase 1 already has the embed_query half ported
     (embed::voyage::embed_query).
     Phase 2 lifts that into the trait alongside embed_documents. The current
     embed::embed_query free function (used by cli::search::run) becomes a thin
     wrapper over make(...).embed_query(...).

     Step 2.1b вҖ” embed::cache (~1 day)

     Per-(provider, model) cache file under data/index/embed_cache/. Compact
     binary
     format (50 % smaller, 2Г— faster load than msgpack-of-f64-lists):

     embed_cache/{provider}--{model}.bin layout:
       [0..4]    u32 magic   = 0x52414331  ("RAG1")
       [4..8]    u32 version = 1
       [8..12]   u32 dim
       [12..20]  u64 n_entries
       [20..]    n Г— (32 bytes sha256 || dim Г— 4 bytes f32, little-endian)

     API:
     - pub struct Cache { provider: String, model: String, dim: usize, entries: 
     HashMap<[u8;32], Vec<f32>> }
     - pub fn hash(text: &str) -> [u8;32] (sha2::Sha256::digest)
     - pub fn load(dir: &Path, provider: &str, model: &str) -> Result<Cache> вҖ”
     returns empty cache if file absent
     - pub fn save(&self, dir: &Path) -> Result<()> вҖ” atomic via tempfile +
     rename

     Bootstrap path: if no cache file exists for this (provider, model) but
     embeddings.bin + chunks.msgpack exist (and cfg.embedding.{provider, 
     model_name} matches what built that index), walk them and seed the cache.
     Mirrors Python's _load_embed_cache fallback in pipeline.py:27. One-shot
     transition aid for users coming from v0.2.

     Read perf: 500 MB binary file load is ~2 s on SSD with mmap + bytemuck:: 
     cast_slice (zero decode cost). msgpack equivalent was ~5 s + 2Г— memory.

     tools/migrate.py updates: write embed_cache/voyage--voyage-code-3.bin in
     the new format (replaces the existing embed_cache.msgpack write).

     Step 2.2 вҖ” embed::throttle (~1 day)

     Port _AdaptiveThrottle from src/ragrep/ingest/embed.py:39 exactly:
       initial 30s, min 0.2s, max 90s, 0.75Г— decay after 3-streak success
     (clamped to
       floor), 1.5Г— backoff on rate-limit (or retry-after + 2s), floor
     remembered =
       current delay, floor erodes 0.85Г— every 10 successes within 1.1Г— of
     floor.
       3 unit tests covering decay / backoff / floor erosion transitions.

     Step 2.3 вҖ” Three provider impls of Embedder::embed_documents (~3 days)

     Each provider gets its own embed::{voyage,openai,gemini}::Embedder struct
     that implements the trait. The HTTP shapes differ but the loop pattern is
     the
     same вҖ” extract a private _embed_batch_loop helper if duplication gets
     noisy.

     Common loop shape:
     - Iterate texts.chunks(batch_size) (provider-specific cap, see table)
     - Sync HTTP via reqwest::blocking
     - Throttle between batches via embed::throttle
     - HTTP 429: parse Retry-After, throttle.on_rate_limit(retry_after),
     sleep, retry up to 5Г—
     - Checkpoint every 500 batches: embeddings_checkpoint.bin
     (u32 n_done + u32 total + n_done Г— dim Г— f32). Resume on restart if
     total matches. Format is Rust-internal (process-local).
     - On success, delete the checkpoint

     Per-provider specifics:

     Provider: voyage
     Endpoint: POST api.voyageai.com/v1/embeddings
     Batch cap: 16
     Key envs: VOYAGE_API_KEY
     Notes: input_type=document. Tight rate limits вҶ’ throttle is load-bearing.
     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
     Provider: openai
     Endpoint: POST api.openai.com/v1/embeddings
     Batch cap: 64
     Key envs: OPENAI_API_KEY
     Notes: Higher rate limits. dimensions query param for
     text-embedding-3-large
       (which is 3072 by default; allow 1024 for compat with our dim slot).
     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
     Provider: gemini
     Endpoint: POST

     generativelanguage.googleapis.com/v1beta/models/{model}:batchEmbedContents
     Batch cap: 100
     Key envs: GEMINI_API_KEY
     Notes: Different request shape; per-instance task_type.

     Output normalization: all 3 providers emit L2-normalized f32 vectors. If a
     provider returns un-normalized (rare), normalize at the boundary so the
     rest
     of the pipeline can assume вҖ–vвҖ– = 1.

     Tests per provider: integration test using a recorded HTTP fixture (or
     mockito) that asserts the trait's contract: identical query вҶ’ identical
     embedding bytes (to f32 precision).

     Step 2.4 вҖ” ingest::chunk (~1вҖ“2 days)

     Port chunk.py exactly вҖ” including the heuristic _approx_tokens = 
     max(word_count, len // 4).
     Do not add tiktoken-rs: the Python uses the heuristic on purpose because
     tab-delimited content (CSVs, code) underestimates with real tokens. Drop
     tiktoken-rs from Cargo.toml.

     - SEPARATORS = ["\n\n", "\n", "\t", ". ", " "] recursive split.
     - 64-word overlap (trailing N words of prev chunk вҶ’ start of next).
     - MAX_CHARS = 4000 post-split safety valve.
     - NO_CHUNK_SOURCES = {bookmark, pin} (both small, never split).
     - Each chunk: id = "{doc_id}:{chunk_idx}", copies doc.metadata + adds
     chunk_idx.
     - Golden tests: pick 5 representative documents from the existing real
     chunks.msgpack and assert Rust chunker produces the same chunk count +
     content as Python (or document any drift).

     Step 2.5 вҖ” ingest::normalize/* (~5вҖ“7 days, the biggest piece)

     Each Python normalize_* becomes one Rust submodule. All read JSONL from
     data/raw/<file>.jsonl (or sidecar users.json / channels.json for slack)
     and emit Vec<Document>.

     Build order (simplest вҶ’ hardest; ship + test each before the next):

     #: a
     Module: normalize::bookmark
     Input: bookmarks.jsonl
     Python LOC: ~25
     Notes: Trivial: title + link вҶ’ Document
     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

     Notes: Needs clean_text + user_map
     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

     #: i
     Module: normalize::slack
     Input: messages.jsonl + sidecars
     Python LOC: ~90
     Notes: Hardest: thread grouping, mrkdwn cleaning, system-subtype filtering

     Shared infra in ingest::normalize::mod:
     - read_jsonl(path) -> Vec<serde_json::Value> (or strongly-typed via serde
     derive).
     - load_users(path) -> HashMap<String, UserInfo> + load_channels(...).
     - clean_text(text, &user_map) -> String вҖ” port the 10 regex patterns from
     normalize.py:16 via the regex crate (compiled once via OnceLock).
     - user_label(uid, &user_map) -> String вҖ” port the name (title) formatter.
     - normalize_all(raw_dir) -> Vec<Document> вҖ” calls each normalizer + dedups
     by Document.id.

     Each normalizer gets a golden test reading 10 representative records from
     real
     data/raw/<source>/ and asserting the produced Document matches Python
     field-for-field.

     Step 2.6 вҖ” ingest::pipeline (~1 day)

     pub fn run(cfg, force, source_filter) -> Result<IngestStats> mirrors
     pipeline.py::ingest:
     1. Resolve embedder via factory: let embedder = 
     embed::make(&cfg.embedding.provider, &cfg.embedding.model_name)?
     2. Load per-(provider, model) cache: embed::cache::load(index_dir, 
     embedder.provider(), embedder.model())?
     3. normalize_all(raw_dir) вҶ’ docs (optionally source_filter-pruned)
     4. chunk::all(docs, max_tokens, overlap)
     5. content-hash diff vs cache
     6. embedder.embed_documents(misses, batch_size, checkpoint_path) (or skip
     if 0)
     7. Assemble full embedding Vec<Vec<f32>> in chunk order
     8. index::store::save_chunks + index::bm25::Bm25::build + save_bm25 +
     write embeddings.bin (concat'd raw f32, atomic via tempfile + rename)
     9. cache.save(index_dir)
     10. Log per-source counts + elapsed
     - Pre-warm rayon at the top so chunk + normalize benefit on the M-series
     Mac.

     The pipeline never names a provider directly. Switching cfg.embedding = 
     {provider="openai", model_name="text-embedding-3-large"} is a config edit;
     no Rust changes. The cache is namespaced by (provider, model) so the switch
     doesn't poison the existing voyage cache.

     Step 2.7 вҖ” cli::ingest::run (~ВҪ day)

     Already stubbed in Phase 0. Wire to ingest::pipeline::run. Print stats +
     elapsed.

     Scope cuts (Phase 2 v1 will not include)

     - Voyage Batch API (submit_batch / collect_batch in embed.py:299).
     33% discount, вүӨ12h completion window. Useful only for first-time bulk
     ingest
     of a large corpus. Defer until someone actually needs the discount; the
     sync
     API + adaptive throttle handles the regular case.
     - Multi-model embedding (multi-FAISS index per query).
     config.embedding.models = [...] lets one index hold parallel embeddings
     from N models, fused via multi-signal RRF at query time. Adds index format
     complexity. The trait + per-(provider, model) cache shipped in this phase
     makes a future v2.5 multi-model addition mechanical.
     - sentence-transformers local embedder. Already cut in the Phase 0 plan.
     - ntfy.sh mid-batch notifications. Useful for hours-long Modal runs;
     defer until ingest runs that long are common.
     - Modal-based remote ingest (modal_ingest.py). Stays Python for now вҖ”
     Modal's Python SDK is the entry point; nothing to gain by porting.

     Parallelism

     Normalize and chunk are embarrassingly parallel:
     - normalize_all: process the 9 source modules in parallel via
     rayon::scope (each I/O-bound on its JSONL file).
     - chunk::all: docs.par_iter().flat_map(chunk_document).collect(). With
     103k вҶ’ 1M+ chunks, the speedup is meaningful on the M-series Mac.
     - embed: rate-limited; sequential (don't parallelize).

     Ship serial first; add rayon after profiling shows it matters. Pre-warming
     rayon happens in cli::ingest::run (same pattern as cli::search::run).

     Why a custom binary cache (vs. keeping msgpack)

     The currently migrated embed_cache.msgpack is 1.1 GB for 121k entries Г—
     1024 dim because msgpack-python serializes f32 lists as float64. Switching
     to the binary format described in Step 2.1b cuts that to ~500 MB and is
     ~2Г— faster on read (mmap + bytemuck::cast_slice is zero-copy; msgpack
     allocates a Vec<f32> per entry). It also makes (provider, model) part
     of the filename, which is the cleanest way to namespace per-model caches.

     tools/migrate.py updates to write the new format under
     embed_cache/voyage--voyage-code-3.bin. The old embed_cache.msgpack can
     be deleted after migration.

     Verify (Phase 2 ship gate)

     1. From-scratch ingest works. rm -rf 
     data/index/{*.msgpack,*.bin,embed_cache} && ragrep ingest produces
     chunks.msgpack + embeddings.bin +
     bm25.msgpack + embed_cache/voyage--voyage-code-3.bin.
     2. Chunk count parity. New chunks.msgpack count matches the migrated
     v0.2 baseline within 5% (small drift from edge cases in the chunker is
     acceptable; document any > 5%).
     3. Search parity vs Python. tools/parity.py against the freshly-Rust-built
     index passes 30/30 queries at вүҘ90% top-10 overlap (Phase 1's bar).
     4. Cache-hit idempotence. A second ragrep ingest with no data/raw/
     changes triggers 0 embed API calls; all chunks hit cache. Wall < 15s for
     103k chunks (binary cache load + BM25 build).
     5. --force re-embeds. Wipes the per-model cache, hits the embed API,
     produces a fresh embeddings.bin byte-identical to the prior run (for
     normalized vectors, the API is deterministic on the same input + model).
     6. --source slack partial. Only re-embeds chunks where chunk.source == 
     "slack". Other sources stay cached.
     7. Throttle behavior under rate-limit. Manually trigger 429 (or use a
     mocked endpoint) and confirm embed::throttle backs off + recovers.
     8. Checkpoint resume. Kill mid-batch (Ctrl-C after 500+ batches), restart,
     resume from checkpoint. End state matches uninterrupted run.
     9. Provider swap is config-only. Set [embedding] provider = "openai", 
     model_name = "text-embedding-3-large" in config.toml; ragrep ingest
     embeds against OpenAI, writes
     embed_cache/openai--text-embedding-3-large.bin,
     leaves the voyage cache untouched. Search still works. Switching back to
     voyage reuses the cached voyage embeddings (zero re-embed).

     Verify: from a clean Docker container (debian:bookworm-slim and archlinux),
      curl ragrep.cc/install.sh | sh && ragrep --help works. From a fresh macOS,
      same. ragrep "auth" --server http://...cloud-run-url works (proves Cloud
     Run binary too).

     Hot-path performance targets

     These are the success criteria for "did the rewrite achieve the latency
     goal":

     Risks & mitigations

     - Flat-search SIMD performance. Hand-rolled with wide::f32x8 should land
     within 2Г— of FAISS's native SIMD on Apple Silicon. Mitigation: Phase 0.1
     spike measures this directly. If we're slower than 10ms per query at 103k
     chunks, fall back to usearch (single-header, mmap, mature; ~half-day swap).
      Decision point inside Phase 0, day 1.
     - mmap correctness on Linux/macOS/Windows. memmap2 handles all three but
     Windows file-locking semantics differ. Mitigation: deferred until Phase 0.2
      cross-compile CI exercises Windows; if Windows mmap is fragile, gate the
     Windows binary on --no-mmap mode (read-into-Vec) until fixed.
     - GDrive OAuth in Rust. yup-oauth2 requires either service-account JSON
     (cleanest) or an installed-app flow with localhost callback. Mitigation:
     require service-account JSON for v1; document how to create one. The Python
      path used gcloud auth application-default login which is convenient for
     the user but harder to match in Rust without shelling out.
     - Async/sync split in CLI. ragrep "query" doesn't need an async runtime
     (one HTTP call to Voyage rerank). Spinning up tokio for that is overkill
     (~5ms cost). Mitigation: embed:: and rerank:: expose both sync (ureq) and
     async (reqwest) variants; the CLI search path uses sync, the serve
     subcommand uses async.
     - tiktoken vs Voyage tokenizer drift. Voyage uses its own tokenizer; we'd
     be using cl100k_base. For chunk-size enforcement (512 tokens) the drift is
     small (вүӨ5% chunk-count differences in practice). Mitigation: accept the
     drift; chunks aren't required to be exactly 512 tokens. If Voyage rejects
     an oversize batch we already retry.
     - Pickle migration robustness. The migration script must read whatever
     pickle protocol Python wrote. Mitigation: the script runs in the user's
     existing venv (which has the same pickle/Python version that wrote it), so
     this is a non-issue. Document the venv requirement in MIGRATION.md.
     - Scope creep. 10вҖ“12 weeks part-time is a lot. Mitigation: Phase 1 is the
     ship-gate. After Phase 1, users get the latency win immediately. Phases 2вҖ“5
      can take as long as they take without blocking value.

     Verification recipe (end-to-end)

     After Phase 0.1 (spike) ships:

     # Extract embeddings from existing FAISS index
     python tools/extract_embeddings.py data/index/
     ls -la data/index/embeddings.bin                          # expect 
     423,329,792 bytes

     # Build the spike
     cargo build --release

     # Spike parity check (uses query embeddings extracted from Python)
     python tools/spike_parity.py                               # writes 3 query
      JSON files + Python top-10
     ./target/release/ragrep --query data/spike/q_auth.json     # expect same 
     top-10 indices
     ./target/release/ragrep --query data/spike/q_deploy.json
     ./target/release/ragrep --query data/spike/q_incident.json

     # Bench
     ./target/release/ragrep --query data/spike/q_auth.json --bench 10  # expect
      <10ms p50

     After Phase 1 ships:

     # Build for current platform
     cargo build --release

     # Smoke test
     ./target/release/ragrep --help                            # <20ms expected
     ./target/release/ragrep                                   # shows splash

     # One-time migration: chunks.pkl + embed_cache.pkl вҶ’ msgpack 
     (extract_embeddings already ran in Phase 0.1)
     python tools/migrate.py data/index/

     # Parity test against Python
     ./tools/parity.sh                                         # 50 queries, 
     вүҘ90% top-10 overlap

     # End-to-end search
     ./target/release/ragrep "auth" -m grep -n 5
     ./target/release/ragrep "auth" -m hybrid -n 5
     ./target/release/ragrep "auth" --json | jq

     # Server mode (uses existing Python server)
     RAGREP_SERVER=http://localhost:8321 ./target/release/ragrep "auth"

     # Cross-compile sanity
     cross build --release --target aarch64-apple-darwin
     cross build --release --target x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu

     After Phase 5 ships:

     # From clean Docker
     docker run --rm -it debian:bookworm-slim bash -c \
       "apt-get update && apt-get install -y curl ca-certificates && \
        curl -fsSL https://ragrep.cc/install.sh | sh && \
        ~/.local/bin/ragrep --help && \
        RAGREP_SERVER=https://your-cloud-run.run.app ~/.local/bin/ragrep 'auth'"

     What stays after Phase 5

     - docs/ (landing page, install.sh, fonts) вҖ” unchanged content, install.sh
     now downloads binary
     - tools/migrate.py вҖ” kept indefinitely so old-Python users can still
     migrate
     - config.toml format вҖ” same TOML shape, fully readable by Rust
     - .env / .env.example вҖ” same env vars
     - data/index/ layout вҖ” same files, msgpack instead of pickle for
     chunks/embed_cache
     - GitHub repo URL (github.com/fntune/ragrep) вҖ” same
     - Vanity domain (ragrep.cc) вҖ” same

     What goes:
     - pyproject.toml, src/ragrep/, uv.lock, Makefile (replaced by justfile or
     just cargo commands)
     - requirements.txt Cloud Run target (replaced by Dockerfile building the
     Rust server binary)
     - All Python deps (voyageai already gone, faiss-cpu/rank-bm25/torch/transfo
     rmers/sentence-transformers/google-genai/etc.)

        1 +//! Per-(provider, model) embedding cache, on-disk binary form
          +at.                                                           
        2 +//!                                                           
        3 +//! Lives at `<index_dir>/embed_cache/{provider}--{model}.bin`
          +. Compact layout                                              
        4 +//! (~ВҪ the size of msgpack-of-f64-lists, ~2Г— faster to load v
          +ia mmap +                                                     
        5 +//! `bytemuck::cast_slice`):                                  
        6 +//!                                                           
        7 +//! ```text                                                   
        8 +//! [0..4]    u32 magic   = 0x52414331  ("RAG1")              
        9 +//! [4..8]    u32 version = 1                                 
       10 +//! [8..12]   u32 dim                                         
       11 +//! [12..20]  u64 n_entries                                   
       12 +//! [20..]    n Г— (32 bytes sha256 || dim Г— 4 bytes f32, littl
          +e-endian)                                                     
       13 +//! ```                                                       
       14 +//!                                                           
       15 +//! Multibyte ints are little-endian. The sha256 keys are raw 
          +bytes (the                                                    
       16 +//! `hash()` helper hashes UTF-8 source text). The f32 vectors
          + are written                                                  
       17 +//! as raw bytes via `bytemuck::cast_slice`.                  
       18  
       19 +use std::collections::HashMap;                                
       20 +use std::fs::{self, File};                                    
       21 +use std::io::{BufReader, BufWriter, Read, Write};             
       22 +use std::path::{Path, PathBuf};                               
       23 +                                                              
       24 +use anyhow::{anyhow, bail, Context, Result};                  
       25 +use sha2::{Digest, Sha256};                                   
       26 +                                                              
       27 +const MAGIC: u32 = 0x5241_4331;                               
       28 +const VERSION: u32 = 1;                                       
       29 +const HEADER_BYTES: usize = 4 + 4 + 4 + 8;                    
       30 +const HASH_BYTES: usize = 32;                                 
       31 +                                                              
       32 +pub type Hash = [u8; HASH_BYTES];                             
       33 +                                                              
       34 +pub struct Cache {                                            
       35 +    provider: String,                                         
       36 +    model: String,                                            
       37 +    dim: usize,                                               
       38 +    entries: HashMap<Hash, Vec<f32>>,                         
       39 +}                                                             
       40 +                                                              
       41 +impl Cache {                                                  
       42 +    pub fn empty(provider: &str, model: &str, dim: usize) -> S
          +elf {                                                         
       43 +        Self {                                                
       44 +            provider: provider.to_string(),                   
       45 +            model: model.to_string(),                         
       46 +            dim,                                              
       47 +            entries: HashMap::new(),                          
       48 +        }                                                     
       49 +    }                                                         
       50 +                                                              
       51 +    pub fn provider(&self) -> &str {                          
       52 +        &self.provider                                        
       53 +    }                                                         
       54 +    pub fn model(&self) -> &str {                             
       55 +        &self.model                                           
       56 +    }                                                         
       57 +    pub fn dim(&self) -> usize {                              
       58 +        self.dim                                              
       59 +    }                                                         
       60 +    pub fn len(&self) -> usize {                              
       61 +        self.entries.len()                                    
       62 +    }                                                         
       63 +    pub fn is_empty(&self) -> bool {                          
       64 +        self.entries.is_empty()                               
       65 +    }                                                         
       66 +                                                              
       67 +    pub fn get(&self, key: &Hash) -> Option<&Vec<f32>> {      
       68 +        self.entries.get(key)                                 
       69 +    }                                                         
       70 +                                                              
       71 +    pub fn insert(&mut self, key: Hash, vec: Vec<f32>) {      
       72 +        debug_assert_eq!(vec.len(), self.dim, "vector dim mism
          +atch");                                                       
       73 +        self.entries.insert(key, vec);                        
       74 +    }                                                         
       75 +                                                              
       76 +    pub fn contains(&self, key: &Hash) -> bool {              
       77 +        self.entries.contains_key(key)                        
       78 +    }                                                         
       79 +                                                              
       80 +    pub fn iter(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = (&Hash, &Vec<f3
          +2>)> {                                                        
       81 +        self.entries.iter()                                   
       82 +    }                                                         
       83 +}                                                             
       84 +                                                              
       85 +/// Sha256 of the UTF-8 bytes of `text`. Stable content hash f
          +or cache keying.                                              
       86 +pub fn hash(text: &str) -> Hash {                             
       87 +    let mut hasher = Sha256::new();                           
       88 +    hasher.update(text.as_bytes());                           
       89 +    hasher.finalize().into()                                  
       90 +}                                                             
       91 +                                                              
       92 +pub fn cache_dir(index_dir: &Path) -> PathBuf {               
       93 +    index_dir.join("embed_cache")                             
       94 +}                                                             
       95 +                                                              
       96 +pub fn cache_path(index_dir: &Path, provider: &str, model: &st
          +r) -> PathBuf {                                               
       97 +    cache_dir(index_dir).join(format!("{provider}--{model}.bin
          +"))                                                           
       98 +}                                                             
       99 +                                                              
      100 +/// Load a cache from disk. Returns an empty cache if the file
          + doesn't exist.                                               
      101 +pub fn load(index_dir: &Path, provider: &str, model: &str, exp
          +ected_dim: usize) -> Result<Cache> {                          
      102 +    let path = cache_path(index_dir, provider, model);        
      103 +    if !path.exists() {                                       
      104 +        return Ok(Cache::empty(provider, model, expected_dim))
          +;                                                             
      105 +    }                                                         
      106 +    let file = File::open(&path).with_context(|| format!("open
          +ing {}", path.display()))?;                                   
      107 +    let mut r = BufReader::new(file);                         
      108 +                                                              
      109 +    let mut header = [0u8; HEADER_BYTES];                     
      110 +    r.read_exact(&mut header)                                 
      111 +        .with_context(|| format!("reading header of {}", path.
          +display()))?;                                                 
      112 +    let magic = u32::from_le_bytes(header[0..4].try_into().unw
          +rap());                                                       
      113 +    let version = u32::from_le_bytes(header[4..8].try_into().u
          +nwrap());                                                     
      114 +    let dim = u32::from_le_bytes(header[8..12].try_into().unwr
          +ap()) as usize;                                               
      115 +    let n = u64::from_le_bytes(header[12..20].try_into().unwra
          +p()) as usize;                                                
      116 +                                                              
      117 +    if magic != MAGIC {                                       
      118 +        bail!("{}: bad magic 0x{:08x} (expected 0x{:08x})", pa
          +th.display(), magic, MAGIC);                                  
      119 +    }                                                         
      120 +    if version != VERSION {                                   
      121 +        bail!(                                                
      122 +            "{}: unsupported cache version {} (this binary sup
          +ports {})",                                                   
      123 +            path.display(),                                   
      124 +            version,                                          
      125 +            VERSION                                           
      126 +        );                                                    
      127 +    }                                                         
      128 +    if dim != expected_dim {                                  
      129 +        bail!(                                                
      130 +            "{}: dim mismatch вҖ” file has {}, embedder expects 
          +{}",                                                          
      131 +            path.display(),                                   
      132 +            dim,                                              
      133 +            expected_dim                                      
      134 +        );                                                    
      135 +    }                                                         
      136 +                                                              
      137 +    let row_bytes = HASH_BYTES + dim * 4;                     
      138 +    let mut entries = HashMap::with_capacity(n);              
      139 +    let mut row = vec![0u8; row_bytes];                       
      140 +    for i in 0..n {                                           
      141 +        r.read_exact(&mut row)                                
      142 +            .with_context(|| format!("reading entry {i} from {
          +}", path.display()))?;                                        
      143 +        let mut key = [0u8; HASH_BYTES];                      
      144 +        key.copy_from_slice(&row[..HASH_BYTES]);              
      145 +        let vec_bytes = &row[HASH_BYTES..];                   
      146 +        let vec: Vec<f32> = bytemuck::cast_slice(vec_bytes).to
          +_vec();                                                       
      147 +        entries.insert(key, vec);                             
      148 +    }                                                         
      149 +                                                              
      150 +    Ok(Cache {                                                
      151 +        provider: provider.to_string(),                       
      152 +        model: model.to_string(),                             
      153 +        dim,                                                  
      154 +        entries,                                              
      155 +    })                                                        
      156 +}                                                             
      157 +                                                              
      158 +/// Save the cache atomically (tempfile + rename).            
      159 +pub fn save(cache: &Cache, index_dir: &Path) -> Result<()> {  
      160 +    let dir = cache_dir(index_dir);                           
      161 +    fs::create_dir_all(&dir).with_context(|| format!("creating
          + {}", dir.display()))?;                                       
      162 +    let final_path = cache_path(index_dir, &cache.provider, &c
          +ache.model);                                                  
      163 +    let tmp_path = final_path.with_extension("bin.tmp");      
      164 +                                                              
      165 +    let file = File::create(&tmp_path).with_context(|| format!
          +("creating {}", tmp_path.display()))?;                        
      166 +    let mut w = BufWriter::new(file);                         
      167 +                                                              
      168 +    w.write_all(&MAGIC.to_le_bytes())?;                       
      169 +    w.write_all(&VERSION.to_le_bytes())?;                     
      170 +    w.write_all(&(cache.dim as u32).to_le_bytes())?;          
      171 +    w.write_all(&(cache.entries.len() as u64).to_le_bytes())?;
      172 +                                                              
      173 +    for (key, vec) in &cache.entries {                        
      174 +        if vec.len() != cache.dim {                           
      175 +            return Err(anyhow!(                               
      176 +                "vec dim mismatch for key {:?}: expected {}, g
          +ot {}",                                                       
      177 +                &key[..8],                                    
      178 +                cache.dim,                                    
      179 +                vec.len()                                     
      180 +            ));                                               
      181 +        }                                                     
      182 +        w.write_all(key)?;                                    
      183 +        w.write_all(bytemuck::cast_slice(vec))?;              
      184 +    }                                                         
      185 +    w.flush()?;                                               
      186 +    drop(w);                                                  
      187 +                                                              
      188 +    fs::rename(&tmp_path, &final_path)                        
      189 +        .with_context(|| format!("renaming {} вҶ’ {}", tmp_path.
          +display(), final_path.display()))?;                           
      190 +    Ok(())                                                    
      191 +}                                                             
      192 +                                                              
      193 +#[cfg(test)]                                                  
      194 +mod tests {                                                   
      195 +    use super::*;                                             
      196 +    use tempfile::tempdir;                                    
      197 +                                                              
      198 +    #[test]                                                   
      199 +    fn roundtrip_empty() {                                    
      200 +        let dir = tempdir().unwrap();                         
      201 +        let c = Cache::empty("voyage", "voyage-code-3", 4);

      207 +

вҸә Write(rust/src/embed/throttle.rs)
  вҺҝ В Added 158 lines
        1 +//! Adaptive rate-limit throttle.                             
        2 +//!                                                           
        3 +//! Direct port of `_AdaptiveThrottle` from `src/ragrep/ingest
          +/embed.py:39`.                                                
        4 +//! Starts conservative (30s for Voyage free tier with 16-chun
          +k batches),                                                   
        5 +//! decays delay after consecutive successes, backs off on rat
          +e-limit, remembers                                            
        6 +//! the boundary so it doesn't immediately probe below the fai
          +led delay again.                                              
        7 +//! The floor decays over time so probing eventually resumes (
          +matches Python).                                              
        8  
        9 +use std::thread;                                              
       10 +use std::time::Duration;                                      
       11 +                                                              
       12 +const DEFAULT_INITIAL: f32 = 30.0;                            
       13 +const DEFAULT_MIN: f32 = 0.2;                                 
       14 +const DEFAULT_MAX: f32 = 90.0;                                
       15 +                                                              
       16 +/// Number of consecutive successes that triggers a delay deca
          +y.                                                            
       17 +const SUCCESS_STREAK_FOR_DECAY: u32 = 3;                      
       18 +/// Multiplier applied to delay on success-streak (clamped to 
          +floor).                                                       
       19 +const DECAY_FACTOR: f32 = 0.75;                               
       20 +/// Multiplier applied to delay on rate-limit (when no `retry-
          +after`).                                                      
       21 +const BACKOFF_FACTOR: f32 = 1.5;                              
       22 +/// Window around floor that counts as "near floor" for erosio
          +n (1.1Г— floor).                                               
       23 +const NEAR_FLOOR_RATIO: f32 = 1.1;                            
       24 +/// How many successes near the floor erode it by `FLOOR_DECAY
          +`.                                                            
       25 +const SUCCESSES_TO_ERODE: u32 = 10;                           
       26 +/// Multiplier applied to floor when eroding.                 
       27 +const FLOOR_DECAY: f32 = 0.85;                                
       28 +/// Seconds added to a server-supplied `retry-after` header va
          +lue.                                                          
       29 +const RETRY_AFTER_PAD: f32 = 2.0;                             
       30 +                                                              
       31 +#[derive(Debug)]                                              
       32 +pub struct Throttle {                                         
       33 +    pub delay: f32,                                           
       34 +    min_delay: f32,                                           
       35 +    max_delay: f32,                                           
       36 +    consecutive_ok: u32,                                      
       37 +    floor: f32,                                               
       38 +    floor_successes: u32,                                     
       39 +}                                                             
       40 +                                                              
       41 +impl Default for Throttle {                                   
       42 +    fn default() -> Self {                                    
       43 +        Self::new(DEFAULT_INITIAL, DEFAULT_MIN, DEFAULT_MAX)  
       44 +    }                                                         
       45 +}                                                             
       46 +                                                              
       47 +impl Throttle {                                               
       48 +    pub fn new(initial: f32, min_delay: f32, max_delay: f32) -
          +> Self {                                                      
       49 +        Self {                                                
       50 +            delay: initial,                                   
       51 +            min_delay,                                        
       52 +            max_delay,                                        
       53 +            consecutive_ok: 0,                                
       54 +            floor: 0.0,                                       
       55 +            floor_successes: 0,                               
       56 +        }                                                     
       57 +    }                                                         
       58 +                                                              
       59 +    /// For tests / introspection.                            
       60 +    pub fn floor(&self) -> f32 {                              
       61 +        self.floor                                            
       62 +    }                                                         
       63 +                                                              
       64 +    pub fn on_success(&mut self) {                            
       65 +        self.consecutive_ok += 1;                             
       66 +                                                              
       67 +        // Erode the floor: SUCCESSES_TO_ERODE successes near 
          +floor вҶ’ 0.85Г— decay                                           
       68 +        if self.floor > 0.0 && self.delay <= self.floor * NEAR
          +_FLOOR_RATIO {                                                
       69 +            self.floor_successes += 1;                        
       70 +            if self.floor_successes >= SUCCESSES_TO_ERODE {   
       71 +                self.floor = (self.floor * FLOOR_DECAY).max(se
          +lf.min_delay);                                                
       72 +                self.floor_successes = 0;                     
       73 +            }                                                 
       74 +        }                                                     
       75 +                                                              
       76 +        if self.consecutive_ok >= SUCCESS_STREAK_FOR_DECAY {  
       77 +            let new = (self.delay * DECAY_FACTOR).max(self.min
          +_delay);                                                      
       78 +            self.delay = new.max(self.floor);                 
       79 +            self.consecutive_ok = 0;                          
       80 +        }                                                     
       81 +    }                                                         
       82 +                                                              
       83 +    pub fn on_rate_limit(&mut self, retry_after: Option<f32>) 
          +{                                                             
       84 +        self.consecutive_ok = 0;                              
       85 +        self.floor_successes = 0;                             
       86 +        self.delay = match retry_after {                      
       87 +            Some(s) if s > 0.0 => (s + RETRY_AFTER_PAD).min(se
          +lf.max_delay),                                                
       88 +            _ => (self.delay * BACKOFF_FACTOR).min(self.max_de
          +lay),                                                         
       89 +        };                                                    
       90 +        // Remember this delay as the new floor.              
       91 +        self.floor = self.delay;                              
       92 +    }                                                         
       93 +                                                              
       94 +    pub fn wait(&self) {                                      
       95 +        thread::sleep(Duration::from_secs_f32(self.delay));   
       96 +    }                                                         
       97 +}                                                             
       98 +                                                              
       99 +#[cfg(test)]                                                  
      100 +mod tests {                                                   
      101 +    use super::*;                                             
      102 +                                                              
      103 +    /// 3-streak success at default вҶ’ delay 30 вҶ’ 22.5 (0.75x),
          + no floor set.                                                
      104 +    #[test]                                                   
      105 +    fn success_streak_decays_delay() {                        
      106 +        let mut t = Throttle::default();                      
      107 +        let start = t.delay;                                  
      108 +        for _ in 0..3 {                                       
      109 +            t.on_success();                                   
      110 +        }                                                     
      111 +        assert!((t.delay - start * DECAY_FACTOR).abs() < 1e-3)
          +;                                                             
      112 +        assert_eq!(t.floor, 0.0);                             
      113 +    }                                                         
      114 +                                                              
      115 +    /// rate-limit with no retry-after вҶ’ 30 вҶ’ 45 (1.5x), floor
          + = 45.                                                        
      116 +    #[test]                                                   
      117 +    fn rate_limit_backs_off_and_sets_floor() {                
      118 +        let mut t = Throttle::default();                      
      119 +        t.on_rate_limit(None);                                
      120 +        assert!((t.delay - 30.0 * BACKOFF_FACTOR).abs() < 1e-3
          +);                                                            
      121 +        assert!((t.floor - t.delay).abs() < 1e-3);            
      122 +    }

      131 +    }

      136 +        let mut t = Throttle::default();

          + вҶ’ 25.3 вҶ’ 19, but clamped at 45                               
      139 +        for _ in 0..9 {                                       
      140 +            t.on_success();                                   
      141 +        }                                                     
      142 +        assert!(t.delay >= t.floor - 1e-3);                   
      143 +        assert!((t.delay - 45.0).abs() < 1e-3);               
      144 +    }                                                         
      145 +                                                              
      146 +    /// 10 successes near floor вҶ’ floor decays by 0.85x.      
      147 +    #[test]                                                   
      148 +    fn floor_erodes_after_streak_at_floor() {                 
      149 +        let mut t = Throttle::default();                      
      150 +        t.on_rate_limit(None); // floor = 45, delay = 45      
      151 +        let initial_floor = t.floor;                          
      152 +        // 10 successes near floor вҶ’ floor erodes             
      153 +        for _ in 0..10 {                                      
      154 +            t.on_success();                                   
      155 +        }                                                     
      156 +        assert!(t.floor < initial_floor);                     
      157 +        assert!((t.floor - initial_floor * FLOOR_DECAY).abs() 
          +< 1e-3);                                                      
      158 +    }                                                         
      159 +}

      174 +const CKPT_MAGIC: u32 = 0x5241_4332; // "RAG2"                
      175 +const CKPT_HEADER_BYTES: usize = 4 + 4 + 4 + 4;               
      176 +                                                              
      177 +/// Try to read a checkpoint at `path`. Returns Some(prefix) i
          +f the checkpoint                                              
      178 +/// matches the expected `total` and `dim`; otherwise None (an
          +d the file is                                                 
      179 +/// quietly ignored). Errors only on I/O / parse problems.    
      180 +fn read_checkpoint(path: &Path, expected_total: usize, expecte
          +d_dim: usize) -> Result<Option<Vec<Vec<f32>>>> {              
      181 +    if !path.exists() {                                       
      182 +        return Ok(None);                                      
      183 +    }                                                         
      184 +    let file = File::open(path).with_context(|| format!("openi
          +ng checkpoint {}", path.display()))?;                         
      185 +    let mut r = BufReader::new(file);                         
      186 +    let mut header = [0u8; CKPT_HEADER_BYTES];                
      187 +    if r.read_exact(&mut header).is_err() {                   
      188 +        return Ok(None);                                      
      189 +    }                                                         
      190 +    let magic = u32::from_le_bytes(header[0..4].try_into().unw
          +rap());                                                       
      191 +    let n_done = u32::from_le_bytes(header[4..8].try_into().un
          +wrap()) as usize;                                             
      192 +    let total = u32::from_le_bytes(header[8..12].try_into().un
          +wrap()) as usize;                                             
      193 +    let dim = u32::from_le_bytes(header[12..16].try_into().unw
          +rap()) as usize;                                              
      194 +    if magic != CKPT_MAGIC || total != expected_total || dim !
          += expected_dim {                                              
      195 +        // Stale checkpoint; ignore.                          
      196 +        return Ok(None);                                      
      197 +    }                                                         
      198 +    let mut bytes = vec![0u8; n_done * dim * 4];              
      199 +    r.read_exact(&mut bytes)                                  
      200 +        .with_context(|| format!("reading checkpoint body of {
          +}", path.display()))?;                                        
      201 +    let flat: &[f32] = bytemuck::cast_slice(&bytes);          
      202 +    let out: Vec<Vec<f32>> = flat.chunks_exact(dim).map(|c| c.
          +to_vec()).collect();                                          
      203 +    Ok(Some(out))                                             
      204 +}                                                             
      205 +                                                              
      206 +/// Atomically write a checkpoint with the embeddings collecte
          +d so far.                                                     
      207 +fn save_checkpoint(                                           
      208 +    path: Option<&Path>,                                      
      209 +    all: &[Vec<f32>],                                         
      210 +    total: usize,                                             
      211 +    dim: usize,                                               
      212 +) -> Result<()> {                                             
      213 +    let Some(path) = path else { return Ok(()) };             
      214 +    if all.is_empty() {                                       
      215 +        return Ok(());                                        
      216 +    }                                                         
      217 +    if let Some(parent) = path.parent() {                     
      218 +        std::fs::create_dir_all(parent).ok();                 
      219 +    }                                                         
      220 +    let tmp = path.with_extension("bin.tmp");                 
      221 +    let file = File::create(&tmp).with_context(|| format!("cre
          +ating checkpoint {}", tmp.display()))?;                       
      222 +    let mut w = BufWriter::new(file);                         
      223 +    w.write_all(&CKPT_MAGIC.to_le_bytes())?;                  
      224 +    w.write_all(&(all.len() as u32).to_le_bytes())?;          
      225 +    w.write_all(&(total as u32).to_le_bytes())?;              
      226 +    w.write_all(&(dim as u32).to_le_bytes())?;                
      227 +    for v in all {                                            
      228 +        w.write_all(bytemuck::cast_slice(v))?;                
      229 +    }                                                         
      230 +    w.flush()?;                                               
      231 +    drop(w);                                                  
      232 +    std::fs::rename(&tmp, path)                               
      233 +        .with_context(|| format!("renaming {} вҶ’ {}", tmp.displ
          +ay(), path.display()))?;                                      
      234 +    tracing::info!(                                           
      235 +        target: "ragrep::embed",                              
      236 +        "checkpoint saved: {}/{} at {}",                      
      237 +        all.len(),                                            
      238 +        total,                                                
      239 +        path.display()                                        
      240 +    );                                                        
      241 +    Ok(())                                                    
      242 +}                                                             
      243 +                                                              
      244 +/// Pull `Retry-After` (in seconds) out of an embed error, if 
          +it was a 429.                                                 
      245 +/// Returns Some(secs) on rate-limit (with possibly None retry
          +_after meaning                                                
      246 +/// "use default backoff"), and None on any non-429 error.    
      247 +fn parse_429_retry_after(e: &anyhow::Error) -> Option<Option<f
          +32>> {                                                        
      248 +    let msg = format!("{e}");                                 
      249 +    if !msg.contains("HTTP 429") {                            
      250 +        return None;                                          
      251 +    }                                                         
      252 +    // Look for "retry-after: <num>" in the body.             
      253 +    let lower = msg.to_lowercase();                           
      254 +    if let Some(idx) = lower.find("retry-after") {            
      255 +        let tail = &msg[idx..];                               
      256 +        let secs: String = tail                               
      257 +            .chars()                                          
      258 +            .skip_while(|c| !c.is_ascii_digit())              
      259 +            .take_while(|c| c.is_ascii_digit() || *c == '.')  
      260 +            .collect();                                       
      261 +        if let Ok(v) = secs.parse::<f32>() {                  
      262 +            return Some(Some(v));                             
      263 +        }                                                     
      264 +    }                                                         
      265 +    Some(None)                                                
      266 +}

      270      model: &'a str,
